O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and have made an end by its expositions and by its declarations.  
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'. 
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is strange throughout everything, so is the science lost and diminished, and nothing remains of its strength except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved. 
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this came the error and the vanity, and are closed the intentions and is alienated the science.  
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I will revive it along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; 
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will bring together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the explanation and preparation of them, as it is necessary. 
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of those that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged.  
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes it to mount in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of veins, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and brains and the number of vessels, and the movement and of moving and resting veins, and their place of origin.  
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work a little. 
et meismement en l’art de main.	and also in the art of hand.  
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say to you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things said before, should guard himself so as not to err and to injure people.  
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	and just as I have seen many times more than these who involve themselves in this science and abandon their science and sense of experience.  
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen a fool who has made an incision of a carbuncle or neck of a woman, and has also cut into the arteries in the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for which so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.  
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I have seen another physician who was treating a stone from a man's body, and the stone was large
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took out with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.  
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called for to treat it, and saw the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and well if one cut it he would die.  
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another wound that took care of the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture there was a wound; 
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	And the poor ignorant healer strained the fracture over the wound as stars by very strong ligatures, and did not leave any of xalene to the wound, and left it thus at the end; 
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded him that he should not untie it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And remained thus that the leg was all swollen and the foot, and came to ruin. 
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I untied it, it was in peace and he felt no pain. 
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But every way the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not heal it. 
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And did not cease the corruption from going through the member until the member was completely lost.  
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another sight who burst open the abscess, and then inflamed it with the malice of its lord. 
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not befit that one touch it with iron unless in such a place where one can remove all that is corrupt. 
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into II divisions: 
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, works where there is peril in many dispositions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril. 
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For which reason it is necessary that you guard against them, so that foolish people may not speak ill of you. 
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in custody, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised. 
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the treatable diseases to a better health; 
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And remove your weapons from that which causes you doubt, and have done in yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other of glory. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his admonitions:  
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	“Take no care for ill-health, lest you be called a foolish mirror.” 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	“I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.”  
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is of fire cautery and of medicinal cautery, and it is the chapters ordered from the head down to the feet; 
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of the instruments, and of the workings of cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work. 
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is of cutting and probing, and of suction cups and wounds, and of the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And are the chapters ordered and the forms of the instruments.  
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is to restore dislocations and twists, and similar things; 
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And are ordered from the head just as far as the feet, and the forms of the instruments.  
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember from the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the help and the nuisance of each complexion. 
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of the help, and the nuisance, is the longest speech and subtle science and the secret responses; 
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And of this speak most sages, and agree to this;  
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I suffice myself little their words, because I fear the length. 
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cauterizing helps universally to all complexion where it has matter, for  it complexes:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This is to know complexions hot sense matter, and complexions dry sense matter.  
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion together matter, they said none and said that cautery is great help; 
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other said the contrary:  
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is of no use to illness that comes from heat and dryness. 
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be cured of a hot illness by heat, nor by dryness; 
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and says he who says the contrary that cautery does great help to a hot and dry illness that comes in the bodies of men.   
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold. 
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.  
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it no time through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in all ways, let no one intervene except he who has practiced it and who knows by long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the space of time; 
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no more fear, even in cold and moist diseases.  
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the mirrors assembled and agreed to the cautery. 
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that  cautery assembled fire is of the secret of cures, and of greater good than cautery of burning medicine. 
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	Because the fire is simple, and does not come out except to the member that is burned, and does no harm to another member if he is named. 
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The burning medicines come from member to another in separating, and bring to the member illnesses of grievous healing;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance kills the patient. 
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not do this, unless there is superfluity.  
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things. 
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself for the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I deprive you of the secret which is revealed in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out illnesses from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts. 
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that it is agreed upon what time the cauteries should be made and when they are to be applied. 
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harms arising are lessened by the help of cautery; 
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and also if the cautery is for necessary pains, except and until they cannot endure the time that greater evil comes to the limb. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish men do;  
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery has no return; 
et il le dient ensi;	and they say thus:
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, for cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries up the humors which are the cause of pain, and it is better than medicine for the speed of its power, and for the virtue of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And a certain thing is that the disease comes never according to the complexion of the patient and its place and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if this is not cauteries administered where there it has little superfluity and moisture, like cauteries of bone for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return.  
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens little. 
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand for what reason cautery is called the last of medicine, and it is so. 
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cautery is worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is cautery the last of medicine because when we administer manners of cures in any disease and they are not worth, then we administer our cautery, and it is worth. 
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it appears well that cautery is the last of medicine, not according to the understanding of foolish people.  
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries of instruments of gold are more effective than those of iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and for the height of its substance.  
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the heat of the cautery does not cause rot, but this is not true because I have tested it and found that it is true in some men.   
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And gold cauteries are worth more than those of iron, as they said.  
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And nevertheless when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much; 
si font au feu;	as they do in fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough impediment.  
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our cauteries of iron which we have found to be more effective in our work.   
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter of the heads to feet, for that the vein be easier to find.  
dou cautere olivaire	Of the olive cautery 
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two kinds done because of a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for multitudes of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases. 
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicine solutive modifying the head III or IV, according to what the virtue and the age and the habit of the patient can suffer. 
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make a hole in the head of the patient.  
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit crossed between your hands, and place his hands on your thighs; 
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	After that, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; 
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and where your two thumbs will come, if it bleeds then apply the cautery which is called 'olivarius', because of this is its form: 
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and do by descending and pulling your hand back and forth turning.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then raise your hand slightly, and look at the spot if you see the bone little;  
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then begin the cautery again until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After that take a piece of silk, and put in soft cotton inside it, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days;  
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After put on above a softened cloth; 
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And leave on as long as the burn is removed. 
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treat the wound with an ointment that is called "tetrafarmaçon", as long as it is healed.  
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they say the ancients, that when longer it stays open the wound, more it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	And for this so help moves. 
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that one must let the cautery as long that part of the bone is burned, and then reset what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say the other that one must let the cautery as long and thrust so strongly one lowers the bone also wide as the whorl that women put in their spindles for this that the humors come out moved.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound long uncovered; 
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after it one must cure and treat.  
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two manners of cautery do not seem to me to be good in all respects, except in certain men where there is a way of fear. 
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I believe that I should leave it.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the head is weakened by the continuous dissolution of nature, as we witness in other members; 
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more wholesome and useful for me, and from this I operate in such a way as to assemble health. 
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in all the head comes chronic pain, and lasts long, then the patient should use herbs and pills that are called "cochie," and of purgation of the head and oils and plasters; 
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we have said before, and it is not effective 
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take heed if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution, and is not too cold. 
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize it with less heat than the one we have said above.  
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After making the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make the cautery at their place that is called "vessels"; 
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and put them in where one puts  suction cups. 
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and align your hand so that you cannot see up to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I shall speak of it later; 
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is fitting that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head 
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain, and it extends to the eye, and the jaw is purged by medicinal infusions, and one has done the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help. 
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then I make cauteries according to two ways, that is to say of sharp medicine and of fire.  
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of sharp medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and remove the rind and cut it into two pieces as big as the jaw, and then make the temple where the pain holds in such a manner that you can place the piece of alum under the skin. 
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it will be placed there, bind it and restrain it well and leave it so for twelve hours.  
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	And then untie it and treat fiercely with garlic ointment, and leave the wound so for II days or III.  
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then put a cotton swab soaked in butter over it as long as possible. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After curing with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see it doing so, do any of the burning remedies that I have written or read how to treat burning remedies.  
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done in this manner. 
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery according to its shape, which is: 
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a key or has one curve at its top, and in the middle a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put it on the painful spot, and hold your hand steady and move the fire slightly for a little while, until half of the thickness of the skin is burned. 
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and gently touch your hand so the artery doesn't burn, which is fiery, and flows abundance of blood. 
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After put cotton in awad of silk, and put it on the place for III days; 
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then I put soft cotton dipped in butter, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed. 
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare," do it all at the tip, and guard against cutting the artery in this migraine which is not ancient. 
de emigraine	of migraine 
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you cure a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and see that the cauteries previously mentioned from medicine and iron do not help it, then you must heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white. 
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And thus reign over the place with a line of half a finger in length, and remove your hand once, and strain that you do not cut the artery and that you do not come to the bone. 
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And guard the jawbone that moves when it is moved, and let the nerves only attend to the movement and that spasms do not come upon the patient, and guard against blood flow from the artery when it is cut, or cutting may cause great fear even to him who does not know, and who is not a student and experienced; 
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work be in the middle way;  
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to restrain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you at its place where it appears in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; 
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery as we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; 
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And this cautery is better than that one and more helpful. 
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of ears from cold.  
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and one has opened it with medicines solutives and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then use this cautery which is called 'point', of which here is the form: 
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After prick all around the ear of the sick person, or around the two if the pain holds in both, and you move a little up from the root of the ear after that you have marked the place to burn. 
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And make ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After care the place until it is healed.  
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth. 
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture which must be cured by cautery is only from those that move phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of the diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make a cautery of appearances that come from dryness and swelling of nerves. 
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this appearance of torture which is silent with phlegm of eyes and expectorations of head and gargles, and that does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: 
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and the other a point of fire on the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; 
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cautery in the part that is healthy, and make cauterization in the part of the ear above a point below the horn of the head, and another one on the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery as long as half of the heart is burned. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery:  
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And is the likeness of the scalpel that we have set before, but it is a bit more subtle and it behoves the knife to be a bit larger;  
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing its place as I have said before, until it is sound. 
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When a stroke is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient does not have fever, then I make four cauteries: 
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle, which is called 'vessel', as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; 
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be cured as we have said before.  
de litargie	of lethargy 
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	To this sickness it behoves to give the patient large doses and pills that clarify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After kings lay the head of the sick man flat, and he puts upon the back of the head the plaster of mustard which is written or treated in plasters 
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of the cautery:  
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if the fire as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is healthy so, good is; 
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it is not so, then he makes III cauteries of the head descending until the neck, and there is a space between each cautery one palm;  
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and cures it like the others, and if you see it joined, and the patient is suffering, then he makes one cautery in the middle. 
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if need be, two others on the two horns, and cures it as long as it is healthy.   
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauteries which are called "olivare", as I have said before.  
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head 
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be purified with herbs and those things we have said before. 
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after rinsing the head of the patient, then do cauterize in the middle of the head and on each horn, and behind and III on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is intense, then do IV cautery on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the care as long as it is healed, and be the cautery which is called "olive" that we have said before. 
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use cautery other than that which is phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to purify the brain with herbs and other cures that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from much medicine.  
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, then one makes gargles and chewing changing the brain often with good meats; 
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's head in the middle, and one makes the cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; 
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is weak and suffering, one makes cauteries as I have said to the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil according to the manner that I have said. 
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, one makes the cautery subtle according to this manner: 
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy are the superfluities or moistures corrupted and phlegm thick, then one cauterizes with such cauteries as we have said to the one who has paralysis. 
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by reason of melancholy are the superfluities declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what is before in the division.  
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After raise the head of the sick one; 
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after make the pad of linen well done, as also the circle, so put it in the middle of the head;  
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the sick one sit crossed, and be held well on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after present the linen, and it is worth smearing of wool fat ancient;  
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and the heat to fire moderately, so that the two if he put it can suffer;   
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after empty the circle from within in the head, and let it cool; 
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the sick one each week once with another good government, as long as he be sound.  
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see them cauterized, making many points on all the cautery. 
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery moistens the brain increasingly; 
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then puts on moistened cotton in butter and fat of gooseberry. 
de l’awe des eulz	of the awe of the eyes  
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe comes first to the eyes by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and do give the patient something purifying the head, and ward off all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more times fasting. 
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After, he commands him to put his head back, and make him cautery in the middle of the head, and make him two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the awe is to the two eyes together, or one if the descent is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and make all the cauteries on all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; 
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And guard against the flowing of blood, and if you see too much blood issue, so restrain it with such power as you have.  
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incision the cautery how you will stop it. 
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And no time is a cautery or hot iron applied below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the course of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside. 
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	And one sees that these are cold phlegmatic superfluities, then I make the cautery as I said at the beginning of the art descending to the eyes: 
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cauterize in the middle of the head, and I cauterize on the two temples, and I cauterize where a hot iron is applied below the two bones. 
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is needed more, cauterize it wisely above the eyebrow with a small cautery. 
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	with two wounds of tears within the eyes  
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient III nuts each 
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after  the king the head, and make a cauterization or middle of olive oil cautery;  
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauterizations with the cautery called 'clavilis' on the two eyebrows, one point below the hair;  
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful of the artery that you do not cover it. 
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called 'clavilis':  
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery called 'olivare'.
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form 
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see so, it [cauterizes] on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let the hand go except until one-third of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said. 
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which pricks the eye  
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to the eyelid, and prick the eye, and one does cautery according to these two manners:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine. 
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. 
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then put the patient on their healthy side. 
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after on the paper of the eyes a figure that is as well as the leaf of the myrtle, and it be the beginning of the sign beside the hairs; 
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then one puts cotton moistened in the clear of an egg and mucilage of pellitory on the eye, then heats the cautery of this which is the form:  
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterize on the figure that you have signed point and point many times, that the hairs be burned there at the place; 
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the healthiness of the work is that you see the paper retreated, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; 
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and leave so three days, then one puts cotton moistened in butter as long as the burning is removed; 
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure of ointment as long as it be healed.  
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this, the hairs come, and the paper is softened then begin again the cautery on that same place, just as you did first. 
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are burnt, cauterize until the paper is lifted to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the eye at all. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of medicine burning is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make of parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and quicklime, each a third, and grind them together well.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it carefully so that it does not cool, then on a board above the form you made like the leaf of myrtle, and put over the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the patient holds only in one eye, then one should work in that one, and if in both as well; 
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put under the eye cotton moistened in the yolk of an egg;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the head of the patient be in your hands and put your hand showing on top of the medicine, and press the pus and the yolk all times that the patient feels a biting from the medicine, because it feels a bite like fire.   
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine with your hand. 
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting will have passed, then lift the weight of awe, and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted as if it had been lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then put more medicine on the place where the medicine has not worked, until your works are equal, and your eyes are set. 
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put moistened cotton in butter until the embers are ashes, after which cure the place of the ointment which is called "dyphenis" and others, as long as it is healed. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to work well on your work with great care that it does not fall from the eyes of the medicine. 
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then begin again the medicine on that one which is softened by the paper properly, just as you have done before. 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	afterward cure until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the leaf of myrtle: 
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to those be your constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not be returned the right way to him whose is the study of this art.  
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the cure of fistula by cautery 
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not help, then it is necessary that you make a cautery to him according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put their head on your healthy side 
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does it lean its head. 
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after put moist cotton in the shell of an egg or in pear juice on the eye.  
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After heat the cautery which is such: 
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is curved at the head like the shape of a vulture's feather, together with that which is the cautery 
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see it, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see fit, it should also be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But all the same, this which is curved is more suitable for your work.  
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After press the fistula if it is open, and drain out the pus and dry it
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, then perform the work, and treat externally the bone; 
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Afterward place the hot heated cautery on top, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part over the eye so that your hand does not move foolishly. 
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.  
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good. 
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, begin the cautery again once, and another if you have need of it, and leave it for 3 days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	Afterward put on moistened cotton in butter, and treat with the ointment of desiccation until it is healed, and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then put on medicine sharp corrosive until the bone is uncovered.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king according to what he would come in his chapter. 
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.  
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Attend to a fistula, and cut its place; 
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after put in the fissure the subtle camphor of which here is the form:  
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it to the quantity of one third of an ounce; 
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand over the camphor firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted resin does not run to its eye; 
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient cotton moistened in wine or vinegar;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the resin so art the place of fistula, and the healthy by miraculous health.   
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good. 
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to administer pus to the nostril, and bring the fistula back into the body of the nostril according to what is fitting in its proper place.  
des crevaices en levres	Of openings in the lips 
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, openings in the lips appear that are called "pimples," and even in the lips of children.  
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these openings as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then use a small scalpel cautery according to this form: 
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place it carefully into those openings until it comes just to the bottom.  
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, cover the area with cerate until it is healed.   
de l’aposteme de la goule	Of the abscess of the throat 
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or uvula, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has made putrefaction and rot and becomes a fistula; 
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit at all:  
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	therefore it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; 
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the bot or opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron cauterizes at the bottom of it, and its last point; 
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, after the cure that we have said in treatments, until it is healed;  
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is healed thus, it is good; 
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if this doesn't happen, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in your chapter. 
dou movement des dens	due to the movement of the teeth  
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and they don't help, then put the chief of the patient in your hand;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After heating the cautery whose form will come after here, in such a manner that you put a chain on the tooth; 
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and set inside the hot cautery carefully, and hold so long that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; 
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After release your hand and restart the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and rinse fiercely.  
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner the tooth which was moving is thus confirmed, and the gum softened restrained, and the moisture corrupted dried. 
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or dampness, and the cures of medicine are not worth it, then there is need for cautery according to II manners: 
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery of butter and cautery of fire.  
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from a churn, and the end in a spoon of iron or steel;  
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after take cotton and wrap on the point of a tent, and dip it in melted butter, and put it on the aching tooth until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see such wool and cotton dipped in cold butter, and put it on the aching tooth, and place hot iron above it until the fire reaches the tip of the tooth; 
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery also called fire is such that you take a piece of iron or steel, and it is thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; 
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, of which the form will come after, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled. 
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.  
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter before applying the cautery, and then pull (it) forth. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:  
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whatever shape you wish, and according to what you are able. 
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the cauterizer:  
des scrophules	of scrofulous sores 
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofulous sores are of phlegm and cold humors, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as described after which comes the form, and have it have openings for the fumes to issue from the cautery on the other side.   
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and put the hot cautery on the abscess once, where it is necessary, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess; 
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so for 3 days; 
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on moistened cotton in butter until the burn is gone;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after care the wound with ointment and bandages until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors overcome on the channels of the body, and even when it comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by dissolving medicines; 
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after that you make cautery to the root of the throat, and guard yourself that you do not come as far as the throat, and do not burn more than a little bit of  the heart;
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After the fire cautery is made to the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be as we have it described before. 
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said before until it is healed.  
de la toust	of the fist 
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and sickness of the fist is due to cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the sickness is ancient, then make II cauteries on the knuckle in their viscera. 
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and the other cautery removes the pain between the two nipples.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be according to the form that has been described before. 
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, make cauteries pricking at all the cautery which is called "poins" for as its form is here before in the illness of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points reach up to XXX, or where they fit. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be at three fingers' widths according to this form: 
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for these are lighter cauteries, because you make three of them at once.  
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation 
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. 
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After be sure the patient lies on his back and on his ribs; 
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after lift the head which is inside the tiltle with two hands of your left. 
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	And if the joint is dislocated inside, then cauterize it with the fire as it has two nerves in this place; 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the liver until it pierces to the rib, and bring the figure of the cautery together with four cauteries;  
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this is made cautery with the cautery which has three nerves, so that the figure of the cauterization are six cauteries;  
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery which has three nerves;
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is joined upon this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries. 
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put the cautery on, rolled with silk;  
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after make the patient rest, and let not move the limbs by long time until he is well fortified.  
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which seldom happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries in pricking.  
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed and the patient heals. 
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold and much moisture until it afflicts his complexion, and multiply catarrh to him, and in ways of accustomed cures and he profits not, then it is necessary that the patient be treated on his back, and extend his legs and his hands. 
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	From this then afterward make three cauteries one below the shoulder blade by the quantity of a die, to all the cautery clavicle, and two cauteries outside the two ribs until the figure of the cauteries is in three angles, and have such spacing between each other that they are not joined together when they will rot; 
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cautery be so perfect that it touches the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without adjustment: 
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see cauterizing with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; 
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach in a spot according to the quantity that you see fit; 
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with the whole cautery which is called "point".  
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the cure that we have had before, until it is healed. 
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver comes pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is forced out of its natural complexion by superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, then it is necessary that the patient be treated on his high-back; 
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and sign of the third cautery according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, away from the hypochondria, where the ribs of man come;  
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and have space between each cautery the thickness of a die; 
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long from the body, and do not press your hand too hard on all the cautery; 
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and burn only the half of the heart, and let the patient be straight on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and lift his arms; 
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your will is so, you cauterize these cauteries of the cuticle, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the whole heart, for you would make the whole body dry; 
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let him not come near boiling water, for the ears are very delicate there, and one can see it. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: 
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong;  
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the membrane, he feels sharp pain. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this cure fails to achieve its purpose, it is necessary that the patient be cared for on his head;  
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then make a poultice in the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to the sunbeam, because of this it is the form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the ear be burned and come to syphac, as long as the puncture is all clean.   
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the cure according to the treatment of wounds until it is healed. 
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And it does not behoove anyone other than those who have studied medicine for a long time and whose hands have cured these illnesses to use this cautery. 
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he may boldly operate, and in all ways it seems to me better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery of pleuresis 
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one must make cauteries for pleuresis with roots of aristolochia, and in such manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristolochia long, the largest that you can find, and whether it is dry, and also as thick and as long as your finger;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soften it in oil, and press it on the fire, and cauterize with this cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and II make small cauteries one by one descending in the part which is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And he cauterizes between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind a little. 
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And he cauterizes in the middle of the hip, and one on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two in the space of the two ribs under the fire cautery which is between the two shoulders.  
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not press your hand, but make it open as if smelling.
