Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And they say that no one ancient used a fire cautery resembling a razor, and heat it and put it between the ribs until it comes to this abscess; 
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and leap out the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. 
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be cured. 
de la mice	of the mouse 
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse of what we have said in the divisions of the cures, and it does not benefit, then they apply three kinds of cautery that are all good. 
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which one manner is that you make three or four cauteries, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have said before.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not hasten your hand with all the cautery, and let the patient be propped up on his back; 
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	And another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder.
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and raise the heart which is placed in the mouse, or the cuts from the patient's side come toward the left, and be the elevation that you raise the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After it burns the two nerves inflamed as long as the heart is pierced from the other side, and then drive out the cautery, and so there will be four. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, burn all the cautery to three nerves.  
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures before mentioned. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy  
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for dropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes". 
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary for you to make four cauteries around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place near the breast; 
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	And let the cauteries be well close to the root of the heart.  
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	Afterward leave the cautery open to prevent putrefaction for a long time, and do not let the treatment of the sick person after the cautery.  
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cautery for the belly is the key that we have in front shows;
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	And that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is set before.  
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet 
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in someone who is hydrophic, and are full of yellow-green fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger. 
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. 
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into the flesh, so that the yellow-green fluid is forced out, and let the cautery be according to this form:  
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After do on each leg two cauteries at the point of the calf. 
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg. 
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries open for a long time without curing, that the fluid may issue.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After the treatment of other treatments that we have said. 
de la menoison	Of the house 
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a belly solution comes from cold and moisture, as much as the retentive and digestive virtues that are in the stomach and intestines are debilitated, and cannot be cured by means of treatments; 
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	And you see the patient suffering greatly and of great virtue, so make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, in the circulating cautery; 
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	And four cauteries around the buckle subtle to all the cautery clavicle subtle, and two cauteries on the kidneys. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the hip, and the cautery on each groin, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, because the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids 
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When hemorrhoids are at the base, or one or more, and they are old and are of large cold and moist humors corrupted, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, if you make cauteries: 
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	III on the spine of the back, which is all outside below the armpit point and point in triangulating, and I cautery below the bud II must; 
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that its stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then to the face one does I great cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and the other on the liver, and the other on the mice to all the cautery clavicle; 
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and leave the cautery open long time.  
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After curing the place until it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh that is called "thelul"  
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut thelul, have the cautery heated which seems like a razor, and then put it all blazing on top of that thelul cut. 
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and leave it as long as the cautery comes to the base of the vein, so that the blood doesn't stop. 
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	Do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each one as we have said. 
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the cures of ointments benefiting until they are healed.  
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the body, there will be more help. 
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly cured wound  
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes such illness that can only be cured by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any one comes fistula, and is enveloped and laid corruption and moistures corrupted, so the does prove to all a tent subtle, and guard that thou knowest to all the tent how much it has of parfont. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heats the cautery which seems I razor, and puts it in the fistula according to the quantity that li tent there entered, and recommences lou cautery until cil corpse porris and corrupted be burned, once, or II or III, according to the quantity of som behoove; 
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and guard thyself from harming the nerve which are inquin, and the great veins.  
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, so guard thyself of these places, and do not make those fuers than in place carnous, and think that she is not mien persons;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After cure the place as long as it is healed, and if the places are clean, and the materials are removed long time, then you know that the places are entirely healed. 
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the materials are not removed, know that the places are rotten, and the bones at the root are corrupted.  
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	And thus as one of these that we shall say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the illness of the kidneys 
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and of great flatulence, and does not take any talant from woman, then it behooves you to make a cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the cautery clavile that we have said before; 
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize it in the middle, then there will be III cauteries in a line, and they will do more great aid. 
de la vessie	of the bladder 
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, both right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the distance between one thumb and another; 
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and make that cautery on fire on the back, where it is needed.  
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cauteries be shaped according to the form previously stated. 
de la marris	of the margin
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception because of it, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are slow;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	And when they come, there is great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	Therefore it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the vulva, as we have said of the bladder cautery, and two cauteries on fire on the back; 
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cautery be of the clavicle, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip  
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous moisture descends to the bone of the hip, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together;  
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and it is found that the place of the department is visible, so you should cauterize the patient above the bone of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the bone as it turns, so that the bone is inside the circle; 
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and let the cautery be like that with which one cauterized the stomach.  
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present to you, make III cauteries of the olive large, and let the cautery be as deep as all the others; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	of the hip pain  
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the socket of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment is not working, and the illness is old: 
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other pills that seem to be good. 
Aprés li fai cautere;	After this do cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of the cautery is according to II manners: 
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery.  
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, of which one is such: 
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the socket of the hip III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them good depth and wide, and have between each cautery a space the size of two, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; 
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	At no time is cautery made in the middle upon the head of the hip, for which there are IIII according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, then cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have before said in the dislocation of the hip; 
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But do in such a manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the flesh be burned.  
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach as far as the thigh nor as far as the leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then one makes II cauteries where the patient says that the pain holds him, and I cautery above the ankle IIII fingers, to the left part a bit.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And let the cautery be a cupped blade, and let it burn the thickness of the heart. 
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two inches of the foot or near it, cauterize where he feels the pain three or four points with the cautery which is called “points.”  
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if necessary, if he does more. 
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he feels the pain below the knee towards the thigh, do cauterize with the cupped or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so long that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do no more harm and contraction to the patient.  
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who made cauteries on the ankle of the foot, and left it there so long that the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the whole foot.  
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a stomach solution from which he died.  
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.  
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the sage said in the cautery of the hip, because this is how it is done, make it like this iron and be at the top as big as a thimble or a little less, and be by interlaces and be from one interlace to the other with space the quantity of a finger's knuckle;
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	And let the interlaces be towards two parts, and let them also be like nuts, and let there be in the hip iron well made; 
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And let it be heated until it is all red and give off a smell, and then put it on the side of the sick hip, and let it be turned over onto the healthy side; 
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and the cauterize once the cautery is on and let it for three days. 
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered long time. 
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of ointment as long as it is healed.  
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery out of fear of its danger, and we see few who use it.
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless those are good cauteries, which he can suffer, and where it is needed. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The cautery of medicine burning is that you make the instrument in entrechatres in which descends the margin of the door, and be it of iron or of steel to a long point, and in its height have two, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a die;
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and be opened from above and below, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After place the hip bone of the patient lying on his healthy side, and after your hand well upon the hip bone; 
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	after put between the two circles of the hot iron which is heated to fire one point, and leave him an hour to ten, and suffer the patient the heat and the burn of it. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there is found medication also as of fire; 
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the medication has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip bone of soft wax, and leave so three days, and put upon butter as long as that which is black from the scald is removed; 
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let him for three days until corruption be drawn out;  
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last aid after the care of ailments until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, then you do the instrument that holds according to what you have done in the hip augmentation. 
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the manner of the hot awe, and I have written it or treated it of the rectification of medicine.  
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.  
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where it has the small opening where the point of a razor can enter. 
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put this pot into another pot well leaden, and put above alkali and quicklime and sweet awe until there is twice as much above the powders than you would have well gripped in your hand;
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let him so until it descends like a fever and stool or as much as possible, then take all this matter, and put it on heat and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be much fever and is administered in various types of medicines and cauteries of other members.  
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	Because it does work like fire, and with other medicines which one cauterizes well the hip as well as turpentine and honey of cashew and heat with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure where one man was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and he praised it very much, and said that no other cure was made, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches here after.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in this manner that you take the green earth litharge, fresh and dry, and grind it well with a little grease, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain holds, and the boil. 
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And let it sit for three hours, and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burn.  
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath as long as his body is a little aroused, and let him enter into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.  
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fire of sheep, it helps a lot; 
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and must be done the cautery in this manner.  
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called foscile. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After take fibers of dry sheep, and wrap them in fire until they are embers, and put it on the linen, and leave it until it is extinguished; 
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and do again in this way, and do not cease to do thus until you think by sense that it comes as close as the hip, and that the pain is ceased;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of sheep". 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back 
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by sitting or percussion or by too great evacuation, or by similar cold matter that is spread out, none of these resemblances are worth cautery, except for those that come from the infusion of cold matter. 
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after those things that the patient is void of stinking pills or other similar ones, that one makes upon his back, where the pain holds, three lines signed with an incisions, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; 
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and be made the cauteries according to the cautery which is called "point"; 
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	And if you see, make III or IV cauteries at the middle clavical cautery according to this form;  
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times comes this disease to little children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow throat when they lie down, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes above the other spines. 
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, if you cauterize it with the cautery of this one according to this form. 
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery scorches each part of the spine equally.  
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery II lines or III, and let the points be near each other. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring the cautery in proximity which is in the space of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints 
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When the pain of joints is from humors which are spread to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, that which the wise call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the foot, then do cauterization to the whole cautery as one claims "point". 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and these happen many times, then do cautery on each knee III cauteries or IV of each part, to all the olive shaped cautery; 
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you have need of more, then do more, but do not hold your hand further than while the head of the cautery is burning.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, so make points around the bone two lines. 
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains no pain at the two joints, then do nothing on each joint and on the hair of the hand; 
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come to the armpits or to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and make good government to the patient and prescribe medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him good governance and purge phlegm, then he will be healed by the help of God.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sciatic nerve 
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When rupture comes in the buttock and the testicles descend to the groin and it is new, then when you see him cured, he must not move that day;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he uses things which make the belly low, so that the intestines descend from his belly; 
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his leg as long as the testicle is repaired, and move them to your groin, and rule of inch below the rupture on the bone of the hip, and all one sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; 
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery of which this is the form: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and it gives off a smell  
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bones to their place; 
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the assistants hold his hand above so they do not return backward;  
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well the thighs on the patient, and put underneath him the cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other upon the hip which holds his hands; 
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the mark with all your might, and hold it straight and keep it there until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then begin again once more until you come to the bone; 
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and beware subtly that the bone does not jump when you make the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it; 
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that by this the patient does not die, or other ills.   
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of the bone, and of big people as large according to their measure;  
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after III days of cure the place of the fire cautery as much as the burn is removed 
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the cure of other ailments as long as he is healed, and lie the patient XL days on his back as long as the wound is well sutured; 
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his dressings be lengthened, so that the boil do not protrude when he tries to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after XL days, when he wants to rise, if he is given a well-made splint, and wear it for another XL days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let him have good rest, that he work little and guard against too great repletion of drink and eating, and of too much heat; 
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And when he does this teaching, he is healed entirely. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall say hereafter the cure of tailoring in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly 
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, make the fire cautery on them according to their quantity, and either burn one-third of the tumor; 
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients said that it must be cauterized with the three-angled cautery according to this form:  
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of incision and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another one below, and hold your hand in the middle of the cautery clamp. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and finer. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in any limb 
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or from striking, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine does not work, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins," and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If it is healed from the first cautery, it is well;  
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	But if not healed from that first cautery, begin another cautery on top of it, because such a custom is that it must heal to the limb that it is nearest to, for which reason it is necessary that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is healing.  
de meselerie	Of the mixing 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The ailments are helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and also the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you see it being cauterized, take care that the patient is at the beginning and if she is cured according to what we have said in the division and does not send nor remain, and you doubt that corruption does not spread throughout the whole sick person, then make V cautery on her head: 
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I put one on the back of the head and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair. 
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	And II on the two horns, and I behind on the nape.  
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	And let your hand so that the cautery comes until the bone, and as long as the scabs come out so that the vapors of the big humors can escape. 
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	And cauterize the mouse according to what it is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the mess is spread everywhere
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it loses manifestly, so it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauteries which we have said or chief, and I cautery on its nape, and II cauteries on the spine of the neck, and VI cauteries on the spine of the back, and I great on the hip and the other below, and II on the two shoulders;  
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and II on the elbows, and II on the tendons of the leg, and I on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; 
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and guard the nerves that are on the rear heel, that you do not burn them;  
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never has one made a cauterization on the bone of the finger, and the other on the bone of the stomach, and the other on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And knows that when more is done cauterization, the more it does help, and moves him profit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as a healthy person does, because the body is already completely corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward, cure the wound with a mixture of flour of violets with honey and other treatments until it is healed.  
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When a swelling comes in any member and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cautery be a point entering into the thickness of the flesh; 
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with ointments until it is healed.  
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And at times one makes a cautery and to the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that numbs the limb, and thus the swelling is removed.
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and nonetheless, let no one interfere unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body. 
de albaras	of  albars 
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the sickness called "albaras" is  enshrined, and the tools of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery in a spot through, according to the quantity of the thickness of the heart, until the redness is removed, and its color has changed.   
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then cure it with flour of veils and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from the colon and blood from alondrine, of each one part; 
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be mixed all together, and be tied with a cloth, and be aired in its place until it is healed.  
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of the sore by cautery 
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When an ulcer comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, if you cauterize it with a cautery which seems like a circle, all around the edge of the ulcer. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nonetheless the sages say that one should make cautery also in the middle of the ulcer;  
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And nonetheless those seem to me not good, because I fear that it may become more ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wished for it to happen any time; 
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And more appropriate a thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called 'circle,' as we have said in many types of cautery. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot die 
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has a malady that is called "adubelati," and it delays in dying, either because of the superfluity which it makes or because of the water of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; 
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see him hasten to die: 
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	therefore, cauterize it around with a small number of cautery points;  
aprés le laisse ensi.	after this, leave it so. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.   
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it burning with the whole cautery, then heat the cautery as this form is: 
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this malady which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the kernel, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning from outside in such a manner that the course of the rot is alleviated. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After this, cure it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure with fire by iron  
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of malady there is which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing else than a rot of a limb, for it gnaws at the members as dry vines do lines.  
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place where it can endure fire cautery, then sharpen the cauteries, small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the illness is. 
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After cauterizing all parts as much as you reach all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, that all that is corrupted be removed.  
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places crushed ointment with oil as long as the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption.  
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ointment generating flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, it is good;  
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if this is not the case, then begin the cautery again on those that remain corrupted from the places. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this malady has at times been cured with hot medicine instead of fire cautery; 
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	But nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure with hot medicine in the division;
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of sprouts that come to the feet 
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that on the feet due to fire a sickness is born which is called “closed” according to our understanding, and it is a very bad thing that inflames the foot. 
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	The cautery of fire is that you heat the iron cautery as much as is a goose quill feather, and make it of good iron to the measure that it may pass over the nail from all sides, and that it have subtle edges;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After he puts everything hot on the nail, and turns your hand all around the nail until it comes to the head of the nail.  
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and he leaves it thus for three days until it begins to rot. 
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then he makes a poultice of wild mallows crushed with wool, and leaves the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then he cures the place with ointment until it is healed.  
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then you must bring them water cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this manner: 
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a piece of iron or steel, or a feather of a vulture, and put it on the nail and the other thing, that is to say warts. 
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and put the iron clamp so that it surrounds all around, then place a piece of hot wax on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the clamp comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water way deep to the root; 
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient endure a bit the burning of the hot water for an hour;  
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave him like this, and it will detach itself from all its roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have removed all those that are in the body, then treat the wounds that generate flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of trembling  
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some tremble from cold nerves, or from quartan fever or another, then it behooves you to make them IV cauteries or IV on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; 
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and for the cautery or weight, and on the stomach with the olive cautery; 
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	if you let it tremble, and hasten the health of the cold sickness.  
des pustules puans	of painful pustules 
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear through fires the body bathed, or painful pustules, that come from large corrupted matters.  
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	so it is necessary at first when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pustule: 
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that the point is seized by the fire, or of long aristige root, or with the lens cautery.  
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes the cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from within forward, but are disrupted the superfluities from which they come, and are healed.   
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut  
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things. 
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very grievous thing to stretch.  
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, you hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain very hard until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no drop issues any more. 
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then put on fire the olive cautery smaller and larger ones until they are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then grasp it, either large or small according to the wound and its location where the artery is routed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is restrained. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your arm above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily another cautery from the fire.  
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is extinguished. 
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside it, and that another evil does not come upon the patient. 
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when without a court of the artery, one cannot well tighten it even when the artery is large, unless by one of the IV ways that we have said:  
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding of thread, or by medicines placed above which have power to tighten blood; 
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and be tied and restrained firmly.  
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring tightening by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot things above, or other similar things, if it does not profit him no.  
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and he has not put any medicine present, then he must place his finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bind it well until it is tightened above the wound and above the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often that it be very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and retracted.   
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And make incisions forward where he has need of cautery and medicine.  
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of wounds 
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases where it is necessary to use fire cautery, or hot medicines, and the incisions, and the causes, and the instruments, and the shapes of the cauteries;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and have put this chapter up to the knees, and I will go in this chapter by the same way for those who find it easier, those who want to.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin these, it is fitting, dear reader, that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason more great caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things. 
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.  
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many kinds of people come to treatments.  
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	so they come from those who are so sick with their illness that they die easily because of the severity of their illness, and the greatness of their evil; 
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and of these one must have fear.  
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And there are some who give you their senses, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am healed; 
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is troublesome.  
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not proper that you allow those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not open yourself foolishly but wisely to those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have taken and benefited from.  
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be converted. 
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and long memory.  
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	My dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and rightness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter for you in chapters, according to what it is before or the chapter of cauteries, which I have devised from the head to the feet, so that you find more easily those that you will need.  
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief full of water 
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this illness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls too hard on the child's head;  
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it comes from a reason that is unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this illness in anyone other than children, and to all of those that I have seen it has hastened death; 
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work to such cures. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew each day until it could not support it; 
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and  the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the sacrum, between the heart and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the work is such that if moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, you make a wide split between the two.   
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and also as long as II us, as long as the moisture runs. 
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, you make II slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form: 
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs that you see the commissures of the chief open from each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it is necessary that you make III slits in the middle of the chief according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw out the moisture completely. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After extracting the slits of drapes and powders, and puts wine and oil in it, and leave thus until the fifth day; 
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then unbind it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the main bandage be fastened, and then give the patient dry meat of a small amount of moisture as long as the limb is fortified and healthy. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look where opens the size of the abscess and the assembly of the liquid; 
car aucune fois est elle devant;	because sometimes it is in front;
aucune fois derrier;	sometimes behind;
aucune fois en destre;	sometimes on the right side;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never once on the left side. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Then cut the abscess opening and fill it with water, and do what you can in that regard. 
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and guard that you do not cut the artery.  
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and blood comes out so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	of a summary 
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease that is called "catarrh" in the eyes or chest, and the illness is old, and the medicine's cure does not help at all, then as the last resort the cure is cauterization with this one that you cut the two arteries. 
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It therefore behoves, when you are about to cut them, that the patient bends his head backwards.   
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after he rubs the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck towards the cloth. 
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are after the ears, and they are then placed back. 
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	then mark the veins of the incisions, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula from two parts, as long as the vein reaches to the bone, and this be by the width of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula under the artery and cut it above, cutting as I told you across. 
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then blood will jump out from above continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery doesn't open at the feeling, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then mark incisions and make them to the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and this that it is necessary to put the blood out is six fingers' width, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the filling of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound: 
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone without any suppuration, then cover the wound with a poultice so that no abscess comes, then strain the wound and bandage it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	Of migraine  
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and acute catarrh, for the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and ancient soreness and similar things, and it is medicated by ways of cures of medicine and all those do not benefit him, then we shall drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.  
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes his hairs of his temples backward, and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not easily found outside than in some men who are too cold.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is put back, restrain the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and apply hot water to the place until the artery appears clearly; 
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula of which here is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then cut it upward with pincers, and carefully separate the webs that are under each part; 
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is thin, then turn it with the point of the probe, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two shoulders. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not jump out all at once.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw blood from the VI (six) parts, up to III (three);
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the closing of the wound, and bleeding does not occur.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut the superfluity which is between the two ligaments in that same hour, and then, if you see it, so cauterize with the cuticular cautery until the bones are reached;  
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and this is the better work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of a hot complexion. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cautery is aid to finish the humors:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for this reason it is of greater aid to the humors. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, that one fills the place with old cotton and puts on top tightly made tents; 
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are removed, so be it cured with dry medicines that make flesh grow and with tents, until it is healed;  
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if without court of the artery as long as you work on it, then hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and strain with your hand that the blood be stanched.  
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this present, then put on the place your cloth as long as the blood is clotted, and raise the place with cold water as long as the blood stops, and be restrained as it is fitting. 
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is mooed and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery trenching from two parts, but the trenchings be well thickened to guard longer their heat. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less its heat. 
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And it must have between the two blades one doit of thickness, and then when you have signed to enchase the two places, and you put the red iron on until it comes just to the bone, and cut the vein in two places;
