et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and let them be kept apart between the two shoulders because it is not completely welded by this cautery at all. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:  
des larmes	of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes descend into veins that are above the temple of the head and it does not benefit from any treatment of medicine one makes, and you see the face of the patient becoming red, and feels or forehead throbbing as if with tremors; 
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and where the skin is damp and so that the hair of the eyelids falls out, and the eyelids are dry, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this treatment.  
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it the ancients "contused cure," and is that you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make III cuts on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; 
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the clefts be like II must take out all the forehead downward to the eyebrow, and the others II as II ribs from above the papers, and guard yourself from cutting into the arteries that are at II ribs from above the papers; 
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of III must across joined.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put the spatula sharp from II parts where here is the shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	From the incision which is from the temple to the second incision 
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the flesh which is between the two incisions to the entire surface that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract the entire spatula.  
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision you put the instrument which is called "cultellar," and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp edge toward the flesh of the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches that which opens towards the heart, and then make another cut in the middle incision until the other end.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw blood evenly, and press the place for the blood drawn; 
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened in wine and oil and vinegar, and guard that no abscess come there.  
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day untie the bandage, and there administer much boiling water, then ointment of basil with rose oil, and other ointments used to heal wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes  
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When with any eye comes acute cataract, and you see the eyes dim and small, and the vision weakening, and the whites burned;  
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and where it is chiefly they feel sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; 
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then know by these accidents that this matter and this cataract comes from many veins, and the treatment for it that is here, if it is true;
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to rear his forehead, then make a great cut between the brow, and another of wide in the cheek. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And beginning from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach to the bone.   
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	And keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; 
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	And when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two edges of the incision and put old cotton, and bandages. 
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	Then bind above cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess. 
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone as long as cartilage begins to form, then treat it with drying things, which cause scar tissue to form.  
En teil maniere:	In such manner: 
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of flower of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster.  
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it on these wounds to prevent flesh from growing everywhere. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears  
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that which is lodged in the ears is one of four things: 
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or animal matter, or a piece of stone, or similar thing such as iron;  
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, such as beans, lentils, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or things flowing like water and similarly and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or some other thing that does not fit in the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun.  
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, distill any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer the extraction; 
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make him sneeze with condiments, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;  
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and hold the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times healing comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come healing, administer to him extraction with subtle pincers, for this is the form:  
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out with the pincers, it's good; 
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If this is not so, then administer extraction to the fine inner part of the small fold.  
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if it does not jump by this means, then make a cane of iron and thrust the head of the cane or perforation of the ear forcefully, and stop that which is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter there with the cane. 
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then the treatment is to make firm, because many times it comes as we have said;  
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come firm in this manner, then take some glue and take the eyes, and put into some instrument which is sharp for that purpose, and put a bit of cotton around; 
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and treat firm.  
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come firm from all these things that we have said, then you hasten to cut open the ear so that an abscess comes out, and spasm;  
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of cutting it is that you first make the patient healthy from the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it hangs;  
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	And let the opening be like a crescent moon, as long as you reach the stone, then the bone according to your strength, and suck it gently with your mouth. 
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment until it is healed.  
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction. 
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it cannot be drawn out, then administer a spatula thin and subtle according to this form:  
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And administer an incision of that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think that the grain is wet because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; 
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.  
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then that drips into the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a cleansing of conditioners first and wets the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie upon that ear itself where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaps out by this means, it is good.  
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If that doesn't happen, then take many stones according to the length of your finger and light ones, and heat them a little in the fire; 
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put them in the patient's ear where it is perforated, and let it be held up by his foot from the other side, and place another stone upon the one that is in the ear; 
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to do this of stone for stone until all the water has gone out, and then it will jump out completely. 
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	And if you see it, then take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and set the other end on fire until the end of the reed is burned.  
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then redo the other part of the joints as long as the liquid comes out completely, as we have said in the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the section. 
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	But if it is large-bodied and can be felt, then administer extraction with tweezers. 
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	And this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section and where we treat distillations, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: 
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If no worms appear, then treat them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the needle that is shaped like this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the most subtle point in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed to all the vein. 
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.  
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, so stop around the vein with cotton as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; 
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if distill your oils and your medicines in the ear to all this instrument, of which this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And be of silver or of iron is narrow below at the small hole, and above over to distill.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation the instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; 
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then put your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the cautery, and the cautery be in the ear; 
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil be distilled or at the end of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and so is the distillation a little bit heated at the fire thus one distills it in the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and guard that it be not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who has no pierced ears; 
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And this same thing happens to men through a swelling of the wound, or of flesh born within the ear, and these swellings come sometimes from being pushed into the ear, if one cannot see it.  
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes it happens the point of fire is lost, and one sees it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Therefore, that which comes in through burning, if it cannot be seen, is of great harm in many situations, and in this one you should put the ear of the patient to the sun.  
et regarde dedens:	and look inside: 
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the apparent hair, then this is how it formed in all of its shape.  
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be acute and cutting before and behind everything full, so that it does not cut the ear; 
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the hair is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut it lightly until that flesh is entirely removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the hair is implanted in the ear, then take a fine razor and lightly heat it on fire, then put it where the body of the ear is.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce lightly, and guard so that you do not wound the nerves of the ear.  
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol;  
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear inflated, it is necessary that you draw the tent and move another moistened tent in cerote that is made of rose oil and wax, as long as the swelling is removed; 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove bleeding which are or treat distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal of papers 
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This poultice that comes from papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary that you extend them with tongs and tweezers, and the scoop a spatula of its roots; 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on their place powdered vitriol.  
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without a decortification, then cauterize it with the subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterize after the incision is useful; 
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times they return, because nothing stays from their roots 
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.  
de la gresle	of the groin 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in papers things that seem groin in shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "graindin," and it is an assembly of thick moisture above and below the paper; 
li ovraiges est telz:	the work is such:  
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take warning if the graindin moves on one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know 
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	do then the wide cut, then the scrape of each part lightly, then take it with tweezers and the scoop 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot scoop it without feeling a bit of the paper, do not harm the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the opening is great, stitch it together, and care for it until it is healed.  
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply force, because the flesh will restore itself quickly and prevent scarring. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and having grasped the hailstone with tweezers,  hold it and press on one side and the other. 
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved by the incision, it does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the hailstone is cut, leave the salty water solution, and care for the area to prevent scarring until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that forms in the thin membrane above the eyes, and this happens more often to children than adults, and it grieves their eyes much, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears well up in their eyes; 
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And for this reason they lie on their faces sideways, and sleep on them, and are their papers under their eyebrows moistened that the inflammation and the appearance have covered with the exina which opens in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two thumbs and feel the exina between them.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your bosom; 
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then takes the linen sheet, and prepares a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exina from each part, then puts it on him; 
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and presses with your thumbs on one and other side, so that the exina is assembled in the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then makes in the middle of the moisture with the pointed spatula a cut wide, and be not more than the wound that one makes to the vein opening; 
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin smooth until you reach the bottom
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many cases the bottom comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract with all your strength between your two fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to the right and left as much as it is spread. 
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep that you do not add in the incision, that you do not come to all the spatula until the eye, that you do not squeeze it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the bottom does not open at the beginning of the incision, then carefully widen the incision slightly until it opens;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten dressings in vinegar and water, and put it on top, and secure with bandages.  
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if it is to such men who grind seed and put it on top to corrupt the moisture that has settled. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure until it is healed.  
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place an abscess, then cure with plasters soothing until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs of the papers  
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When in papers hairs arise adjusted other than the nature, and are spoiled, they harm the eyes, and bring many diseases like accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, as much as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; 
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and it is the cure according to IV manners:  
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cautery altogether fire, or by medicine sharp according to this one that is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done or by incision and stitch or by canes, according to this one that I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient on your own, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand.  
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is turned, it is good; 
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put a needle into the whole thread above;  
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and be it beside the margin of the paper or where the hairs grow beside these hairs, and pull the thread upward to the whole paper, and turn it to the razor; 
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, under the hairs adjusted, to the whole spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small; 
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then place on top of the paper a figure of an eye, as the leaf of myrtle, and anyway it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is divided into all.  
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it is necessary, one should cut a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is. 
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make a total of spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear up to small. 
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the awl in one of the two corners where the kernel is, and then peel it all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle to all the wool thread fine, and wipe the blood, and make air-dry the superfluity of the hairs above the two eyebrows to any sticky things, if you wish to do this. 
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if this is not so, if you have no care, then leave the stitch and the hairs until three days or four. 
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without stitch of drying and constricting things, because the paper revives to the adhesion of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitch is moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear. 
et si a une autre maniere:	and if by another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and that you draw the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at three ounces wide according to the shape that is here. 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut what rises over the small forces equally according to the form which is here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you lack the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle or one with thread, and put it in the middle of the figure.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And put the other thread beside the large tear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble between the two threads equally;  
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin over what you have marked, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed.   
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cress and similar soothing ointments;  
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted. 
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	so it is necessary that you use what we have said of the incision; 
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure of wounds is according to this form:  
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you would convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make two ligatures by art, and two subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are;  
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as two parts where you hold the threads; 
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble the one and the other subtly above what surmounts the paper of the eye, and restrain the two ligatures from the two parts formed;  
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it so for several days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and carry itself, until it comes away by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If he is late, if he does it with force, then treat him until he is healed. 
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is soldered, and if the paper has been lifted, and they will no longer prick hairs; 
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the shape of the two canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide.  
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you prick a subtle needle, and it puts the silk thread soft and subtle; 
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then assemble the jaws and tie one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then arrange in the chase the other thread of silk briefly, and tie the chief of the two threads. 
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head on your own healthy one. 
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And be facing the sun so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and small work. Then put the needle into all the chase in the root of the hair near it, and make it pierce through the paper carefully as long as you pull it above the natural hair; 
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the root, and put it back into the wound if there are one or two or three or more.  
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then pull your hand until the hairs come out of the entire wound on the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the wound away from its bottom all along the line that you have arranged, until the wound comes out of the hole above and you see it with your eyes.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Therefore if you treat the wound and thread it, and close the eye and let it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and flesh grows above.  
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany them with long hairs of natural wool, and let it be lifted along with it, until they grow longer, and then lift it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called 'aleacrati' or the rot comes to the eye, there are two ways it appears.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One natural, and one unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through sudden wounds, or incisions, or cauteries, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way to treat it is that you split that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside a linen pad, and tie it until it is healed. 
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not proper that you use in the cure of them things that dry and restrict 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, then the illness returns worse than the first.  
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but work with softening things, such as fennel; 
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose of water or aloe and linseed seeds be cooked, and diacoylon ointment melted in any oil, and enclose a tent, and treat with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form that it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said are nothing but treatments of this illness so that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the char that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is called 'axacrati', and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wound and split and cautery and similar things; 
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of the work in it is that you prick a needle, in which it has the double thread, and you put it in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the thread comes into the two shoulders of the flesh; 
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then having the flesh above to the whole needle, and the cut to the spatula wide.  
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is fitting, it is good; 
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If those are not, then take the scraper and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits or cuts inside the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the shoulders of the two splits be the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and be made angles so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has the name « I greiche»; 
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that his ribs are raised and out of place, from what follows on the paper, then adjust the two separated parts, and stitch them with a thread of wool. 
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it with those that we have said about softening medicines, and dressings, until it is healed.  
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a cut or suture or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision beneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before;  
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then insert between the two leaves of a bandage, as I have said. 
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one must do the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything of all their power how it does return the figure to its natural form;  
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for work and instruments in many dispositions.  
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this soldering happens to men's hands in such a way that the paper above is glued with egg white, and cannot move or do its natural works, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up. 
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and the extent of pinches, as long as you cut what is stuck to the spatula carefully, which should not be too thick nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer that the spatula is too thick and blinds the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision be, with which you scrape the assembled one, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is healed all of that assembled, and do not at any time in the salty eye water, and the lifting of fresh water, and of collyrium. 
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put over the eye wool moistened in honey; 
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use the collar and things inside until it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the angle is according to II manners: 
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and similar to the hard silk fabric, and another which is not at all nervous, but is similar to white frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and one burns it, it cannot be done.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both appearances begin towards the large tear duct, and cross a little here and there until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your hand, then he opens his eyes. 
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as the pliers of small pleats, and it upward.  
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put upon it hair of horse, or of ox, or of cow, and the thread strong; 
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a bit and insert it into the angle, and pierce it through with the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and bring it upward, and sear all the hair along the side of the angle which follows the small muscle and silk to the hair until the head, then cut away the remaining part at the root of the tear throughout the whole spatula finely and with small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear so that through the incision does not come the body of tears commonly.   
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and no time is the angle extended solely to the thread as we have said.  
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	after the scraping one has all the spathe of what this form is: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the pricked point is not pierced.  
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision put in the eye a bit of ground flaxseed, and from the collar made of lead, and let it until the other day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure that which is necessary until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put in the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines. 
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light bit sharp according to this form
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the finger carefully above it, and if you see that it does not lessen and the pain increases, then distill from your mouth into the eye a colure made of litarge and red colure and finely ground sel, and plug the eye until the next day; 
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as an abscess, then apply poultice, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh near the tear duct harms the eye due to great annoyance, then suspend it with a small hook and cut off a part, but not too much, so that no tear comes out; 
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill in the oil collyrium red which is made of lead ore.  
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the charcoal that arises on the iris 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red charcoal, and covers the iris and rests on the eyelids and turns them to the fire, and seems like a rose of balance. 
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work is that the patient puts his head in a sound place, then the worker opens the eyes, and coils all that charcoal with suitable tweezers to those, and sustains it with strength. 
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first charcoal, and go on cutting all the way to the end, and be careful that you do not blind the eye during the work. 
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be of the spatula that we have said in the incision of the corner and to the small forces of which one removes the white part, as how the form after this chapter it demonstrates. 
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then use the oil of garlic crushed or you distill red cochineal and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top the oil with cotton wool mixed with a bit of egg white, so that it is sure to form a hot abscess;  
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it does not remain there, and the skin surrounds it, and you doubt about the hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess. 
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as long as it is healed, and thus do until the flesh is set in the oil by this method.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you apply the cure of each weak oil to the natural way; 
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in the work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from the work. 
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Several are veins red that are covered on the eye, and they take from sight their work and weaken the eye every days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary that you first look at if the eye, in which it is, and apart from, and there is no other malady besides only the seb 
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then you apply in this manner: 
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient that he put his head in your healthy one, then suspend those veins to the whole body according to his wisdom, and let the threads be subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two threads by degrees in the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then you wind tightly those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins outside of the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatula, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut any other veins 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you will have done this, distill into the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt that which remains of the scab. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot gather all of it in that hour, do a poultice on the eye with things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is appeased and the abscess is assured hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed; 
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mirror is called “arissati” fistula:  
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it with cautery and with a burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut into the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instruments of which this form is made. 
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "sharp head", and it is made of fire iron to the head's front, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:  
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is reset. 
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place of drying medicines.  
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the parts are soldered together, and flesh grows there, and the body of the bone is soldered, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not renew or become inflamed, and no bad accident comes to it, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this is not the case, if there is no other means than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the wound according to this form: 
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And it is that you uncover the bone the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the forest according to this form, and let the shoulder be of iron in three angles, and let the shaft be thinned up to the chief as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through that which comes into his in this way if he holds his hand on his forehead; 
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows back and hardens the union, it will go to the forehead; 
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	so it is a lighter thing for the patient.  
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the issue of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open throughout all and they do not come to trouble to the nose, nor diminish, then it is necessary that you bind the patient. 
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then cleanse, then place a suction cup or haverel without wounding to suck, then put upon the eye a liniment made of wool and aloe and frankincense and sarcocolla, and then restrain the eye, and emplaster it above with bandages and cloths.  
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths sufficiently soft, and double each one in IV, and then put one upon another according to the quantity that the eye has need. 
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then restrain from above with a hard bandage, and begin again the suction cups to suck without wounding;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the suction cups and leave the eye restrained day and night, and if the liniment softens, then it is necessary that you restrain it much.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then bone the join after the day and the nut, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good. 
se ce non;	If this no;  
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then begin again the poultice and bandages and the bone and the leeches until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the unfolding of woolen cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruption comes in the woolen cloth, then open it, and there come forth pieces like the grain of resin, and is esperatable to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it cover, the work is such that you thrust a needle in the root of the lower part until the top, then thrust another needle where there is the double thread from the lacrymal; 
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement; 
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the wool around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put upon the other eye half in an abundance of egg;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it remain until the child falls with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed. 
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and at no time should the wound be restricted by the grape on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye shows a great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes out from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and lower the eye, and enter it immediately. 
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.  
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bow that is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water. 
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it so that you see the bow coming up to your eyes; 
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then be careful, and do not let it descend and become disordered the light, and let the patient see things as he used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend from below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the bowel is not apparent as we have said 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	if you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and feel on the cornea where it joins with the conjunctiva and the crown, as long as the bowel protrudes; 
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is protruded, instill in the eye hot sharp water mixed with honey, or sharp water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have shown the appearances of the waters in their division, and what it is necessary for to consider.  
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, facing away from the sun, and tie the healthy eye and hold it very tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of the eye to your left hand if the eyes are left, or to your right hand if the eyes are right; 
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument which is called 'almagda', or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; 
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then put the point of the instrument beside the crown by the width of a finger in that white part of the eye to the side of the tear duct, then push the instrument which is called 'almagda' skillfully, and thrust your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the hollow thing; 
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is fitting that the measure of the almagda's path be at the midpoint of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black part;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the eye;  
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone in this paper for the clarity of the corneal veil, and then place the instrument up to there where the water is, then express it below one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, if the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.  
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rests the little one, and if the water ascends the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and she does not ascend, gently withdraw algada rotating your hand  poco a poco.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in water a little of silk gum, and leave that eye inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put outside the eye plugged with wool or cloth soaked in rose oil and honey, and tie it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on a mixture above with an abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit," which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce thus only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep in, but make it subtle, then put almond as we have said. 
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And at the completion of the work, equip the patient with a poultice beforehand, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place. 
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	And be free from all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then he unties him in this very dark house, and tests his sight, and makes him see some things, and then he puts the bandage back on until the seventh day. 
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it is not good that you do these things in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you apply this, because the water rises hastily. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the dressing of this which soothes the abscess. 
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is soothed, then untie the sight and put upon his face the little rim to cover for any day, and be again in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then he leaves the house little by little, and becomes again in his state;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that none of disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they did alchemy with almonds, to which they added water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients. 
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it is a new thing.  
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almonds, for those who do not know them see them. 
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they are of grain properly:  
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the chief be like a bird's head of this same subtlety, and the last one in three sharp angles. 
de la char sor le neis	From the wood, on the root
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	At no time do roots of wood grow together in different ways, for that reason there are none which seem like scorpions with many feet; 
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such ones where the wood is cracked of bad color, and if the wood has a good color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that kind of wound which is sore, and not gaping, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; 
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and throw the onion on that wound, and the fumes;  
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then carefully take with a sharp and subtle spatula what you can sustain to it until you know that the wound is all cleaned 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains which cannot be taken, then open it with all the sharp and light instruments so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if there is a boil or abscess, apply a poultice as it is proper; 
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if it is malignant boils, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is seared and all the wounds are removed, then pour on either hot water or wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the nose works, and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is sound. 
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments do not come to cut. 
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Therefore, it is necessary that you put a thread of linen slightly thick into it, and let it be tied with our hands, and have between each knot space  one or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's shoulder into the wool in his hand and pull it out smelling until it comes through the nose into the mouth; 
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times do children like this at school, and it is easy for him who wants to do it;  
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart carefully as we who are wool;
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the nose has corrupted that flesh, then pull out the wool, wipe the blood, and moisten the wool in Egyptian ointment, and put it back straight into the nostril as before; 
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of flesh; 
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then place on it a bandage of wool for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them.
