et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which one distills oils and medicines onto it:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a funnel, and the lead similarly.  
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see fit, make a closed funnel, and let the instruments be full for purging the head;  
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle to hold the head when one heats the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	from that it draws onto the skin  
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times on the head appears a disease called "tellum," and it grows and becomes very large, so much that it is a terrible sight to behold;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and the bone all out, then put on its place the cautery or the ardent medicine; 
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays to cut it until it is large, then take ward if it is hard, of dull color, of poor feeling;  
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if one does not touch it with iron because it is an ulcerated abscess, for when one cuts it any time, much evil comes to the patient; 
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not dull in color, and you see that one can completely cut it, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with drying and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the abscess is cut and sewed 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these work-like cartridges, it profits little, for in no humans. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, first see if the wound is fresh with all its blood. 
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then join the two lips together with a suture, and treat it until it is healed.  
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their core until they bleed, then join the two lips together with a suture, and restrain them, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood, and ground incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on the powders a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly. 
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In men's hands  happen inside the lips abscesses hard, seeming like grains of wheat, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Therefore it behooves you to turn the lips, and split open each knot, and take them with tweezers and cut them in every part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then put on their place after the incision of powdered vitriol, as long as the blood is stopped; 
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it heal itself, and cure its place with dry things until it is healed.   
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times  flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so it behooves you to support it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and leave the blood to clot
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the place vitriol ground, or other powders restraining and drying; 
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, which happens many times, then cauterize it a second time; 
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery; 
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments for cauterizing.
des sordens	of the [burning] irons
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled to the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, sores which are ugly and rough.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes they are [the] tooth black and yellow and towards (a direction), as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and they are the tooth stinking.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	so it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his chin be in your saint (a term of respect), and raise [or open] the teeth or sores as much as possible until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And thus do of blackness and greenishness, and jaundice and other spots, as long as they are mottled; 
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes those that are at the first layer, it is good; 
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have all removed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have need of diverse kinds of instruments for removing them, according to what the work shows, because the rasp used to remove outside teeth has other forms than the one used to remove between the teeth;  
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to draw out as much as you can, because one should not do otherwise;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a most high substance until on's has no excuse for failing to draw it out. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to drink milk, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he believes it is a toothache, and drinks milk from the healthy tooth. 
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	And nevertheless the pain does not depart for this, as long as the evil is present, because we have already seen it happen to our patients. 
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are well certain of the tooth aching, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth entirely. A spatula strong to ward off the gum on all sides; 
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your two tweezers or delicate pincers at the first pock and pock, until it is well loosened, then firmly affirm the tweezers.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And let the shoulder of the patient be in your holy between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out freely, then take any of these instruments and put it inside each side lightly, and move it as you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, then it is necessary that you fill it with dressings, where the holes are; 
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you extract it subtly with pliers, so that it does not break when extracting.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And it is necessary to work very carefully around the gums to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act as the ignorant healers do, who by their haste and boldness break sometimes the chariot, and do not bring it to what we have recounted; 
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring sometimes by the incision of those great sickness from the roots that remain, or because of the chariot that they break, as we have often seen. 
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or oil and salt.  
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, as often happens, apply a powder of vitriol to the place. 
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And if that does not work, cauterize it.  
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments, as to how one pulls teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; 
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large limbs so that they do not bend when working, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold tight. 
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the working area, it is necessary that you put on top of it moistened cotton in butter every day or two, until the bone is softened, then insert the pliers called "algefri," so that the bone seems like a beak when it is handled.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and inside they are made like a file, and this is its form: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali," which is to say a chisel, so this is its form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And it should be thick and large so that it does not break, and if the root pops out through those, it is good. 
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If those do not, with the help of all your instruments, of which the forms come after here:  
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two reins, of which this is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in the fashion of teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great pliers, of which here is the form: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be thick so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are.  
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted. 
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the wise masters subtle ones find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such maladies where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others, and if one breaks not the cartilage or other bones, or it hurts, then he seeks the instruments that are proper, which I have told you, and help with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but that it can be held and removed. 
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then restore the place with suitable medicine for those, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument: 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural body, and the shape is ugly, and even in virgins, then it behooves you to know if the teeth are born after the teeth and are not in their right place, and one cannot file them or smooth them: 
adonques lou raie;	Therefore the filing;  
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is joined with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and it is similar to a small beak, and be of sharp iron at its summit: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope peck and peck in hands daily for the hardness of the tooth, and for those that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then use a type of file as here is its form: 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; 
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in filing a tooth bit by bit in hands lightly, so that it does not move until it chips;  
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the filing at the end to absolutely nothing, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When a front tooth aches, either by percussion or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on it when he chews without pain, and you have cured them with restraining medicines, and this is of no use;  
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then it is necessary to restrain it with a thread of gold, because the silver wire turns green and spoils, but gold never changes.   
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be medium neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; 
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see the teeth crowded together, then take the thread and bring it doubled between the two sound teeth, then put the chiasmus between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you come skillfully to the sound tooth on the other side. 
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then begin the covering again up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and skillfully, until it does not move at all.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the chiasmus of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and place them between the sound tooth, and put it so that it does not bleed the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it thus tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone, or the threads slip, then restrain it with another thread.  
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it stays and serves thus throughout its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls, then it is put back in its place, one by one, as we have said; 
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and no one should interfere who is not skilled and experienced, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from bleached bone, and it is put in the place where there is a deficiency, and it is restrained as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the root of the tongue  
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this root which comes under the tongue or naturally; 
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a wound soldered  
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the works are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; 
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve of the tongue, as long as the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is hardness or numbness, and this is a sign of injury, then put the probe and cut in the wide area that ligament. 
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and keep that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath;  
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done it, raise the head and neck of the patient with a sponge or a cloth of water and cold, then put under the tongue a tent of linen. 
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and the bandage the patient each night, so that the wound cannot close. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, put on top of the area powdered vitriol;  
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with the sluggish cautery, which is good for this. 
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with another treatment until it is healed,  
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it of a reddish or black color or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, because it is an ulcer; 
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then apply the sponge, and scrape it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on both sides; 
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the wound does not heal to your work, then put on powdered vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work as long as you extract everything thoroughly; 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then raise the level of ash and soil, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes inside the throat come boils that are called “godaths,” and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful:  
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If they are hard abscesses of small size and dusky color, do not touch them with iron at all. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron at all, nor for the bleeding. 
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it is rotten, and then you will break it open, or it would burst by itself;  
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and the root is subtle, then have prepared the instrument to cut, but first look whether the abscess feels warm and is appeased.   
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head be in your hands, and open the mouth and place the instrument between his fingers, and press the tongue down with all of the instrument.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be of silver or iron fine as well as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Cannot you press the tongue to all these instruments, and you see the abscess, if you take the needle and place it into the marrow, and drive it upwards more than you can. 
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not draw anything from the tissues with it, then cover the instrument from this, which is the form that seems like a force. 
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and nonetheless the head is curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs for this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be sharpened on one side, and blunt on the other. 
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut one of the marrow, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and plain water, and if the evacuation of blood occurs, gargle the patient with water, or decoctions of pomegranate rinds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped. 
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal until he is sound 
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and no times are abscesses born in the throat other than the two tonsils, so cut them thus as the two tonsils equally. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I medicined a woman of an abscess that she had born inside the throat, that is to say the abscess of small size; 
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had I well nearly closed the whole throat so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was stopped, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained thus one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had been driven into two furrows by its two openings.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then, and put in one the incision, then drew forth the pus and a great portion of bowels; 
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then made another incision in the other opening of the two, and opened her mouth and pressed down her tongue;  
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after having drained the abscess with these poultices, and having cauterized a part of it, 
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus was unplugged the conduit of the throat in the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut at that abscess for a long time; 
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; 
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I closed it and cauterized it inside the throat;
ensi demora sens croistre;	Thus it remained without growing; 
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from those parts, and only God did what came after me.  
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the grape is ripe and it is swollen and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular"; 
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is smaller and round, then it is called "grape".  
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the head of the abscess is appeased, and it is thin, then you must cut it; 
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is rounded assembled and is not long; 
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a rusty color or black, so it is necessary that you make the incision into it.  
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It therefore behooves, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and of its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument about which we have made mention above. 
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the awl into the uva, and treat it with vinegar, and cut to the II instruments that I have said in the incision of the II almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; 
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech;  
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and treat it until it is healed.  
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, you should use an instrument to cauterize the senses that cause fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head on your healthy side, and then presses his tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and confides with very sharp water so that it is not too thick nor too light; 
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And in employ the head of this instrument, for this is its form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have or take a hair or on which one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine on the grape; 
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles move from his mouth to the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the fleece; 
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand to all the medicine and press on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it turn red and the bites of the medicine are calmed;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it on any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton into the canal above, until the cotton dries on the grape; 
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and fall after IV or V days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to begin the fire cautery of medicine again, restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine. 
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be rinsed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until it is healed.  
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision. 
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamine and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and put some water in it, and let it boil; 
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and on top of the pot have the instrument prepared according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And be it of silver or of iron, and let one of the shoulder blades be put in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the vein, until the eye is dead. 
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the eye begins again, until it dries out, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, because many things happen. 
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And make not this further than at the decline of the hot abscess.  
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a vein and put inside the head a piece of egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not have too much heat. 
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Because the egg white does not let the vapor burn the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it has been applied to the throat bone or spine of fish, or any thing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore it is necessary that you draw what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all your instrument, so that you see move the thing. 
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what does not appear to you and is returned into the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach.  
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Perhaps if the thing is thrown out by vomiting; 
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; 
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie it to the sponge, and then swallow it; 
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	And when it arrives at the place, it will swell, and then you will draw further.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not come further than what we have said, take the instrument of plank according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter the throat, and have the head held high. 
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, so that the whole does not close up, nor push inside the bone. 
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And it is better that the patient themselves pushes the instrument, because they know where the thing is hard.  
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If he pushes down, or he draws it outwards with all of the instrument evenly, until it is fully out. 
de la sansue de la gorge	of the cutting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No time is a remedy for the wound, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when those do not help, then look into the throat of the patient in the sun, after you have pressed his tongue with the instrument that I told you about. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, treat it with all little forceps, or subtle pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a dog's hair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put fire at the end of the dog's hair, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient stands of water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take full a glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and put it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often. 
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the patient feels the water, he will spit.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if she does not spit as we have said, then fume the patient with asafoetida, to the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the grape; 
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will purge without vomiting.  
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are burning coals, and let the bottom be covered with a pierced cloth in the middle, and in that put the head of the instrument; 
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then put your fumigation in, and the patient puts the head of the pipe into his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes until the palate. 
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And the bloodletting will now come forth, and if it does not flow, then begin fumigation again many times. 
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and drink no water;  
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And thus it is necessary that she be cured by this treatment.   
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats bloodletting is, when it can be seen, similar to bent pliers for entering into the throat.  
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has the sharpness of a file, so that whoever takes it, they cannot let go. 
et vez ci la forme:	And here is the form:  
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to those who remember afterwards in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size. 
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two manners one of which is in its own likeness, and from that which it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if abscesses should not be pierced until the boil is ripe according to its completion;  
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if to such ones it is necessary to pierce when they are mature and do not ripen according to their completion, like abscesses which are near the joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets it be as long as it is rotten, by chance the ligaments and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or if the abscess is near the principal member and if you delay the piercing until it ripens, it will harm the principal member; 
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the foundation, pierce it thus when it is ripe;  
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not appropriate that you pierce an abscess before complete digestion, except for the one close to its base, so that it may not be further inflamed and become elongated inside, and there comes a fistula. 
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and may not heal in a long time.  
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is done according to its completion, and this is when the pain is calmed, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the loosening and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary that you make the perforation where it depends more from the abscess, and where it opens freely. 
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be long and in the middle of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where it has no flexion. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that are dislocated, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the puncture open as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, then the body of the worm will be lengthened from it, and it is full of much filth. 
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the lips and deepen it.  
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess which are perceived according to the breadth of the body, according to what the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small openings;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if it has such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the heart and cover it; 
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become like a curtain, and is deadened, then it is necessary to do as one does with boils; 
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if it has such ones that are cut into three angles, and if it has such ones which one covers like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of anger;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if it has such or one makes a round incision, and other incisions and seeming cutting. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, as if it were a superficial abscess, you must pierce it fully;  
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and it has become swollen greatly, and you pierce it, if do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a portion. 
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing from it directly;  
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times, large to small, until all the pus is gone; 
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Likewise if the patient is of feeble virtue, or a woman carrying, or a young child, or an old man decrepit.  
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes bursts forth with the exit of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you are not worried about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if wash the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; 
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it is a flat incision, administer pads of linen or old cotton; 
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, you must put a pad in each one so that they come against each other; 
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin and have sewn it together, then you must fill it with old cotton or lint scraped from linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; 
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the abscess will heal and treat it with ointment until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the flow of blood happens in your work, so administer cold water and ease it, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, administer governance and treatment, and the powders that I have said in this book. And if it is during winter, and the part or the abscess is very nervous, then you must put on pads and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; 
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in this state and the parts are fleshy, then it is necessary that you place above them soft cloths in water and oil, or in wine and cooled oil, until the third day, as we have said. 
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it, as is proper, until it is healed.  
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: 
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have told you how one should go before the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.  
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where boils on the head come small abscesses, and they are manners of ours that are in cloths, as the joiner of a hinge, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such that they have moisture as well as boils; 
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are some that are hard and stony in their size, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary to it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the hip are such that you should consider all instruments which are called "entromissoire," because their form comes here afterwards, what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so lift it from above with a long stick.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, because it returns again when one leaves it alone; 
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present 
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day.  
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and cover those who remain from the dampness. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know well that it does not remain damp. 
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with ointment as convenient, until it is healed.  
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds in fatty tissue, cut it according to this form, of length; 
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and insert your probes and its lining from all sides, and put all your care into draining the pus where it lies.  
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery does contrary, then do what I have told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is purulent, and with cutting and caring as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting above the purulent abscess and the moist one is lighter because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if to some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of those which had abscesses that I opened or chiefs of an old woman;  
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess also like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break; 
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had done any of it, they would have made the wound as well as with a stone.  
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses or chiefs, it was that those which come at the chiefs of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that mucus flows out. 
et les cure si com il covient.	and the cure as it is proper.
des scrophules	Of the scrofulous ulcers
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come in other parts or of the body, and are bad, and are joined together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its fold, like the pustule and abscess of the chief, as we have said; 
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the resemblances of these scrophules are many.  
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in which therefore you see good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves from each side and is not at all sore to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the duct, and is not very deep.  
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it is proper that you cut it from above, and the skin is removed from each side, and the two lips of the heart are brought together with sutures, if you need it, as we have said in abscesses of the head.   
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and treat it point by point, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let it not be scraped too much or too deeply, so that your hands escape, and do not see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.   
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powder that stops blood, and hold the wound. 
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.  
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then if there remain any small pustules, cut them and remove them with your finger.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the pustule, it is not necessary to cut that pustule at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread and let it hang, without harming. 
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then that there is no longer any superfluity for the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk the juice, and the count as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more. 
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it thus as that said before, in dependence, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption. 
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, then the ointment cure  preventing flesh, until it is healed.   
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; 
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and it is the scripture of their word.  
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have squint-eyes, it is fitting that the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" be cut.  
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And one does not make help by those, because all the veins and the passages of the sick are to those who have abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the almonds.   
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three circles or four a small slit through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage. 
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those who are so cuttable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long enough.  
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to the whole incision, then cut the keel until it comes to the channel;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and shun the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; 
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the mucus of the channel that flows out from the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice; 
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a while.  
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed from which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound near the heart, and sew them entirely together, except for the cartilage. 
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.  
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is in the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus is kept from death; 
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the sickness is passed, and it is passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and care for it, until it was healed; 
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.  
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took the knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called for the healer, and I found him as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and knew well that it had not been cut vein nor led forward except to the throat, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and so I bandaged the wound, and cured it until it was healed; 
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there came to the lady nothing but that she was hoarse of voice, and returned after to her disposition;  
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for because of this I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "goiter," and it is a large abscess in the color of a bruise, and it is much in women; 
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental.  
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	In the natural one there is no engine. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat in us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And if there is fear, it does not suit to work to do more than in the one that is small, and prove and search all around the introducer: 
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as our fat, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as we cut the ours, and the trail at all its top, if there is one.  
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And enclose well then, and cure it as it suits, until it be perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many manners of ours there are, which I will say all the appearances of;  
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it suits that I say all the difference that is between our and exit. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that exit is sometimes feverish holding, until the boiling has passed, and is accomplished the rotting;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Therefore rests the fever and the heat.   
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a fluid, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes large.  
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to their appearances, whether gray or moist, and many colors as I have said in the division.  
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of this disease that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument that is called "entromissore," according to what its form will be or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of incising abscesses as we do is that you prick or moisten them more than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the interpositor, and take care in those that jump out.  
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever color it has, do it as I have said of other abscesses; 
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introduction moisture comes, know that it is fat, therefore make it in a cross, and take it with pincers, and gently scrape it on each side and guard the coat where it lies so you draw it healthy with the new. 
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it healthy, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.  
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it returns to us many times. 
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if some remains and the wound grieves you, then apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and strain the wound, and put above soothing things, a hot poultice, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the abscess is large, then sew the two lips of the wound, and cure it from that which generates flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein opening is contrary to you or otherwise hurry and use the place of powdered vitriol, and let it lie for two days or three, as long as the wound suppurates, and rests the boiling of blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover what remains from outside. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the  in-introducing instruments, and they are in three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small; 
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three ways of them: 
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like needles with which one sews the sores, and they are of citrine iron, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are more proven from black plumbum to enclose the curves of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and are of III ways: 
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the openings.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the incisions are of many resemblances, as you see here: 
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if incisions which have II curves of III ways also;  
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if incisions which have III curves, and are also of III ways; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if incisions which have II curves, and incisions of one curve only, and are of III ways; 
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.  
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these which one makes are trenching, and there are some which do not cut further than one part, which we scrape the veins with, for that reason one does not cut the vein nor the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introitors are the lancets put back in handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; 
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three ways: 
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see; 
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one should only use them in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar parts;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never is another instrument small, resembling the peelings of fists, according to this form, for which one leeches blood; 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and place it once in its place that is suitable for cutting veins and arteries, and never return according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never do they swell the breasts of some men when they begin to be corrupted, so that they appear like a woman's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should be according to this form of this line b. to g.;
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then join the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed. 
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the mamacle leans downward, and is softened by its size like it does with women, then make two incisions above, in two similar slits.
