de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g..
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and those things that are necessary in the cure, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, for the patient does not want to rest, or for the loss of blood, then it behooves you to fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it so until it mends the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the asses
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas which have ribs, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then use the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment afterwards to it as long as it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of a scrofula, then make it as we have said in incisions of scrofulas, and if the wound is rent inwards, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin above it is sewn together, many times abscesses come about, and this also happens to the vein that has been inflamed and abscessed. 
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you know this is because of the artery, then the abscess will be long and spread out;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you will feel its pulling.  
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when this is because of the vein, it appears red and swollen from without.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, even when it is under the armpits and elbows and neck and in many other places, and is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore it is necessary to use the treatment of fire, and he who is in charge should also use it, and in those who are inflamed by an artery that is cut from above the skin long; 
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the waist with quick movements, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered; 
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then put a needle beneath it, and make it pierce until the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in II lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in the temples; 
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point the place which is between the two ties with an introducer as long as the blood that is there issues forth, and let it be clean the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure that injures the bow, until the tie hangs; 
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure those with ointment coming up to them, as long as they are healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand those that you can from the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle beneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be the double thread, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie up the abscess, as I have told you, or join one of its parts to the two shoulders with a thread; 
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not far enough, then reinsert another needle through all the thread under the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places. 
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut open the abscess until the superfluities are out, then cut away the superfluity of the kernel and leave what is tied.  
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer treatments of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips, and in all their joints where there are abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and is more disposed without pain; 
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is forcibly restrained, the patient feels pain, and it is not felt throughout the body, but beneath the heart; 
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it moves well in every direction, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	for chance, he might go into a contraction; 
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one who is at the top or on the forehead, it feels the skin to the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; 
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a thread and remove the skin, then clean it out and suture the wound, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its appearance, and the root is subtle, and the head large; 
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are some small ones and very large ones;  
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw the man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and were cracked open, and pus oozed out of them.  
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI ⅓, and the work in the incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the article is white and moist and with a fine root;  
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if it cut with a wide spatula, and be in your presence the fire cautery. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For at the cutting comes many times too great bleeding, and if the blood does not stop well, then hasten to cauterize.  
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a thread of silk well made, and tie the articulation as we have said, and let him leave it for days;  
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the silk thread as long as it holds the articulation, and heal by means of it without labor; 
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, then fear to cut it even for the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return;  
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the flesh which is of a yellow color and poor without blood and milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess which has broken open, and I will come to its treatment after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound has healed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery of wound or fissure of the syphons, and is on the belly and in some of the swellings as they have in other wounds, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the sheath and by the opening of the bulb, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from different exits.  
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its two ends it rises up, and then returns, and by chance it may be tight, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it at all; 
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, then it opens by these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and is filled according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you observe whether its appearance is for the blood of an artery, or of a vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So you must let the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bulb, then you must order the patient to keep his arm straight, and be stretched all straight, then reign in everything around the belly; 
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to gently hold between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with the spatula, then bring half of the abscess above to the whole great incision; 
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let it be held in place by the linen band. 
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the half of the abscess extended on the linen, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine. 
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the linen, untie it, and bring the intestine to the outside of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, take it with the incision, and cut off the excess. 
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, go gently around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross so that you make it pierce. 
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in IV places above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave their place until it rots, and the dead flesh falls off by itself. 
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then cure it as it should be, and treat the abscess as we have said. 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it is right, and close the place. 
dou chancre	Of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the appearances of sores, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one should avoid the treatment of iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us say the sore arises in the marsh, and great caution must be taken in its treatment, and ancients have said that when a sore is in a place where one can scrape it like a sore which is in the nipples, and in the buttock, and in similar places, and it should be entirely removed when it is at its beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, you must not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any. 
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever healed it before me.  
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black coles. 
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then let him heal if there is a manifest fullness, then make the patient healthy again in place to do the work; 
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then throw your incisions or ulcers, and the hair of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything. 
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow out completely, and firmly press the place with your hand or anything, and if the bleeding contradicts the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it as long as the blood is extinguished. 
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure of other cures until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron. 
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only lit;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch with iron in these II resemblances:  
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and hypoarche, because it is a mortal thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	therefore when you medicate this resemblance of dropsy which is called "eclitse" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as a cough and solution of the belly and similar things; 
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if you do not touch with iron, because there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	And if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other illness except dropsy alone, and is neither too young nor too old, then do this work.  
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Raise the patient upright on your hands, and the ministers press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the pelvis, then take the spine spatula according to this form:  
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	At its point, and altogether it should not be so deeply inserted that it can come to the intestine when one inserts it, and do not let it pierce. 
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look if the dropsy is in its place towards the intestines:  
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If it is necessary that you cut above the bud, III does right below the armpit.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then your cut should be on the left side of the bud III does.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	And if it is because of the moisture, let it be on the right side, and it is not appropriate that the patient lie on the split so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place; 
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and push it out, and raise your hand to the whole spatula between the skin and the sifac as much as when you are scraping at the quantity of a nail or inquirin.  
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the sifac until the spatula comes to the place where it should be, and this is the place of the water, then push the water out, and put this instrument back as much as this.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a fine silver chain, and is of iron or archaut lighter, and has in the lower part a small hole. 
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on costs one side, III holes.  
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	And II of one side, and I of the other; 
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And the head is cut as a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes cut the feather with:  
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top is the alemale, so that when the instruments come to the point, it descends now onto the instrument. 
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Empty therefore half or the third part, for if you empty more than is proper in this hour, by chance the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death. 
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	But empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the disposition of the virtue of the patient signifies, and his pulses; 
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then treat the instrument and retain the point, and it is retained now by the heart which stops the hole that is on the syfac, for this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner. 
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then begin the instrument again another day, if you see the patient suffering these things, and treat with water a small quantity.  
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do this no day, and keep from heating until it remains but a little bit of water. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you give him much water, then treat with burying or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and it will get better. 
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And treat with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No time is born a child who has no opening in the shaft, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, he must immediately discern with great care the entire spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put or pierce the subtle cloth of plank, and tie it and keep it so for three days or four, and when he wants to make urine, then be removed the clot, and do pee, and then put it back. 
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and perhaps this is not necessary, because the urine coming forth does not let it close. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, so are medicated with the balm of plantain, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the prepuce in its place are pale, because none are born with the prepuce at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before pulling their penis upward; 
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come to the end, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies often on his back, and the head of the penis and the scrotum are lifted like a feather so that the prepuce falls in the middle as it should. 
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care of blood loss which comes often, and if it happens, then the person who is skilled in staunching blood should treat the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times this ailment comes to the shaft, and is an appearance of ugly flesh. 
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and in it there are malignant and non-malignant ones;  
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	so it behooves you to prick them with a fine needle, and scrape and clean them all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment.   
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with Diaphynicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of bad color and discharge, then you must bring it a cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have scraped it, and if the ailment is in the body of the shaft, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it behooves you to remove the ailment which is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is healed, then its cure defer. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it together, make sure the head of the bone is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its shank and groin. 
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it is necessary to shave away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from the rind of quince and verbena, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery helps with two arrangements together: 
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, for the removal of blood, and for corruption.  
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the bone is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you put or drive a chain of lead into the bone, and piss the patient's urine upon it.  
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And when the skin is raw at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, or where there is an ulcer or abscess, then it behooves you to scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the cords are loosened, and the tip of the penis is free on all sides; 
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	And if it is a grievous thing to speak of these, then it behooves you to scrape it with a spatula, little by little, at the head of the penis and the skin; 
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then gently separate them, and put in between them a fine linen cloth moistened with cold water, so that it does not become raw again;
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not the same as other wounds; 
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Nevertheless, when we do this work of our will, and properly to children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the most gentle for healing. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have more than what we have acquired by experiment.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have wanted the greatest part of masters and healers who performed circumcisions in Dal, and with force, and with a whole knife. 
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If they were to cut the foreskin because there are two layers, and by chance one is cut above and the other below stays. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or it must be cut again, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is called Dal, the tip of the member is not well ensured. 
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	And in the purification of the anus, by chance the fire escapes, and the work runs away, and many times they are born so that they don't need purification, and I have wanted it.  
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification that is done with force to the whole line of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	Because when you press your hand, they are equal in length throughout the whole soul tenses. 
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	But that the child should be well enclosed within the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	And be the manner of the first work as this is that you make think the child, if he understands, that you do not to him force only to tie the thread around the rod so only, and then do make him rejoice in all the manners that you can; 
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then do make him stay between your hands straight, and return the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; 
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then thrust your hand to the rod and blow or heart, and the drive in up as long as the head of the rod be in;  
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then purify it well of the filth that is assembled there, then tie the place signed with a double thread, then tie under one pock to the other lien; 
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	And hold it as II dues by the second lieeure to the pouch and to the index, and cut between the II liens, then lift the head upwards gently and drive the head of the rod;  
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood run drop by drop, for it is the cure. 
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and over the powder I drape it with a cloth of a boiled egg yolk tempered with rose water, mixed with rosemary oil good and fresh, and let it remain until the next day, and treat it with another treatment as long as it is healthy. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces in the clarification is this: 
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two shoulders should be held and should be sharp, and the shoulders also as large as the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of the clarification is when the cores inside are at the incision; 
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore it behooves you to extend it to your fingernail so that the pus makes an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then cut it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they exceed three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, let him leave it as long as the abscess chafes is appeased, and scar lightly. 
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you cut it as much as you can move, and keep away from the part of the penis, it will not harm him at all. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore cure the place of things sound wound with powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut too much of the heart, and it goes upwards, it will not harm. 
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is of a stone's lodging, or of blood congealed, or of a bowel, or of fatty flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone in its location or at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let the feet be placed on the back, and extend his belly from above his back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can. 
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and therefore the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released and; 
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer an extraction to it with all the instrument that is called "syringe", of which this is the form:  
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and be of silver subtly light feathered like the feather of a bird; 
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and be the handle a palm long and a half, and be subtle at the head.  
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the issuing of the urine is that you take the doubled thread and tie it at the head a piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the excess of the wool and put it to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; 
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards toward the head; 
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and the patient feels it come to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because of who leads or where it goes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then extend the thread throughout all the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and wash the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood come in the bladder, or there is rot gathered, and you see it distilled with sharp and medicaments, so do it to all the instrument which is called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has III openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; 
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the legs are covered so that the medication is such that it well stops the penis without addition, if one can suck out the moisture, and push when necessary; 
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see fit to place your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and treat with the thread that is inside. 
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you will draw the moisture to the catheter, and then firmly reinsert the thread inside.  
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	then the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it. 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one cleanses the bladder:  
si est ci:	it is here: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or lead, and the head is higher.  
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below to the groin where the connection falls. 
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture with which you wish to cleanse the bladder inside it, then tie it between the two breasts using a thick doubled cord, and warm the moistened bag over the fire. 
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the tip of the clyster into the rectum, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture coming, until the patient feels that the moisture has arrived at the bladder.  
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	And if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make it a circle, and pierce it roundly within. 
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then put the strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dial, and put inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument. 
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.  
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have just said in the division the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And we have said the difference between stones engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in which stone one must work by cutting; 
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis; 
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell it to you plainly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; 
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and I open the harene, and it tightens the patient's penis, and it pains him many times, and then it disappears.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and with many of these leaps its foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is light the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is as the middle to those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and dislocate them and move them downward, so that the hip descends to the level of the bladder, and it comes away from its high position sometimes.  
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands supported, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downward. 
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then grasp it and touch it inside.  
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the hip in that space, then hasten now to cut above the hip. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall upon touching at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult who has completed puberty. 
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and shove it in its foundation, and grasp the hip, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it at the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press upon your loin, and put it out at the fire where you wish to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin which is under the testicles in the part where one makes the cut; 
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then he puts in the spatula cutting, of which this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make between that which is between the testicles and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; 
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight above the stone, and your loins be close or foundation, and let the cut be transverse so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; 
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance the pressure if the loins which is or foundation, that it leaps outwards without work;  
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	And know that there are such stones which have angles, and margins:  
si est griés a issir;	If they are broken to be removed; 
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is one that is soft, appearing like a gland, and rounded, whose exit is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	To those then which have angles and margins, make the incision larger; 
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not come out, then it behooves you to extract it with tweezers that are also like a file at the top, so as to squeeze the stone until it does not escape.  
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you put underneath the instrument subtle and curved at the top;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge I the opening, and if the blood does not come, strain with vinegar.  
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stone, first push the largest to the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the tract, and afterwards the smaller ones if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be stitched up, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:  
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	either he dies, or the urine comes back through the way the wound cannot heal. 
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless you exert yourself to drain it, or to break it with pliers, until you extract it in pieces;  
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have accomplished your work, smear the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and restrain it, and put over it a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then support the patient on their neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you set it free, if there is oil and water, then treat it with dyacin ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corruptions, and a clotting of blood in the bladder, and because of this the urine is retained, which is known in such a manner that without suction with the urine: 
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Therefore pour your drugs into the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and cause harm; 
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then raise the wound with water and oil and soap, and help him in all ways that you know, until he is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you tie his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is or conducted from the penis, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot issue; 
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the care of what I say thus, that you measure it many times, is one excuse for measurement by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I iron rod according to this form and let it be three angles fixed into one stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stones, so that it cannot come back into the bladder. 
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then put the bit in the shaft gently, until it reaches the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And turn the bit in your hand at the stone poke and poke, as long as you can feel the stone on the other side. 
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If the urine comes then press your hand upon that which is remaining of the stone which is within the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then it is broken and leaps out with the urine, and the patient is healed.  
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie the thread below the stone and the other above, then make the shaft straight against the stone between the two liens, then extract it further, and untie the lien, and cleanse the congealed blood which is in the wound. 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It happens that stones are found in women, and if they ever occur, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three things: 
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;  
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman well knowing who reveals her (parts) to others, even when she is chaste.  
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; 
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is that perhaps the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, for which it needs to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity arises to this, then you must take a midwife well knowing, and at pains find one, and if you cannot find one, then no matter how subtle a chaste virgin; 
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and presents a well-wived woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and he commands her to do what you command him of the examination of the stone; 
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: 
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it befits him to push her finger or foundation and search for the stone; 
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then she forces it under her finger, and he recommends that she put her finger or hand on the patient, and search and press her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it befits her to move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is seen appearing, and feel the stone in that part; 
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his loin above the hip or below, and let the waist be first small. 
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then push the loin into the waist, if you feel the hip so close to the wound as long as the hip can issue further, and know that many kinds of hips are: 
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and which have reins.  
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the wound does not close, put on it ground vitriol, and hold it for an hour until the wound is stained; 
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, as long as the hip is further, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of the hip for men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	And if the wound is bleeding and it's from an artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and bind it with bandages and don't start again those things, and leave the stone and don't milk it at all, because by chance the patient could die. 
puis cure la plaie.	Then heal the wound.  
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of blood is appeased, and the tissues become hard, then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramice aquouse is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syrup, which is out of the yolks of eggs, that contains the egg. 
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	And it is called "syrup", and never properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is the other egg;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and this is the skin of the region between the white (syfa) which we have said. 
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and those do not happen at all, no.  
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is so weak that it comes to the joints, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never does it come from percussion on the regions, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is declining in yellowness, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more: 
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white syfac as we have said, then it is the abscess reopens, as long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the regions, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper tissue, then it is the abscess reopening with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white (skin), one feels it well 
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe all the intropositor quite well, for its form is before
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what then comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to our power and the fullness of his body. 
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then place him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put beneath him many cloths;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the scrotum; 
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula lead, and cut the skin of the scrotum among them long up to near the groin, and let your incision be completely straight dividing the skin of the scrotum until the white (skin), and scarify subtly according to your power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the sty into the fluid at the wide opening, and extract all the fluid, and then put your dressings, and stand the sty upward. 
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the head of the coals, but only the sty;  
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut all or in parts evenly the costus from him skillfully, that if you do not cut it well wisely, it will return the fluid. 
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the eye-lid was in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the sty;  
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then assemble the two eyelids of the head of the coals with a suture, then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the eye corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; 
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut the cone to the entire suspensory ligament, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the point is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; 
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If you cut the other part just as you did the first one equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound a half-soaked rag in rose oil. 
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put outside another rag soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two cones, and put cloths doubled above them, and bind it above all the ligament according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and employ them of wool wadding according to this semblance and be assembled by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the shoulders rests on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the armpit.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two chiefs above the two angles, and let the restraint be all assembled in the buckle of the arm.  
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And at no time is this branch of cautery medicated in place of iron cutting tool, and it is that you prick the subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the water is uncovered; 
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	So take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac with one incision, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut in every way that you can, as long as you are scraping all of it;  
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and keep that the fire does not touch the sac. 
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And know that this work is more healed;  
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and moves guarding against the flow of blood, and avoids that the works of cutting. 
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing opposes you, or abscess, or running of blood, or another thing, cure what opposes you, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, administer perforation as I tell you, and when you are certain by the signs that we have said that the water root is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat. 
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess in the part below to the whole spatula wide, and put the perforation through the long of the body; 
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	And let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out.  
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave for it to run out the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	And if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put in a pen or the instrument with which we treat the water of the dropsy, whose form is before. 
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and widen the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and thus will pass the days of the patient. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this root there is fear in many cases, so it seems to me that it is better to leave it. 
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess.  
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I therefore say that many abscesses come from the body, and even so in the joints; 
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is by many causes. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to know by excess of acid and hot, which is spread to the joints, or from percussion; 
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it finds no pain, and is a painful abscess. 
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance there are some painful and dangerous abscesses, and of a bad color, and sometimes come from the outside of an artery or from inflammation of a vein.  
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from the outside of an artery, then it is recognized by the position of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it is not right that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	The one which is made from inflammation of a vein is recognized by its position at the touch of the fingers, and one can well make an incision on this appearance and on the other sores.  
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And that you cut the heart of the sores, then it is in front and the tail further down, and deliver the suspensory on all sides of the head.  
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the head is already joined with these sores, then it is necessary that you cut the head and the heart. 
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is near the skin or in those that are within the vessels, then you must deliver all of that tent, and wrap the top roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the bone is or its rear, then it is necessary that you cut it all and remove the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, then use the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and in wine, then the cure with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is a boil enveloped in an envelope resembling the bourgeon, with the softening of the edges, and the patient cries out sharply when it moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this disease is just as dangerous as the one before, and nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the edges down to their groin, and cover the entire vessels that are near the penis, and stretch them out.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut with a sharp spatula through the vessels in width until they are open, and then scrape from each side, just as we said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then he inserts a needle where it has the doubled thread, and ties it to the first place where the vein came, and ties it straight to the other end.  
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then he cuts them in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and removes the corrupted humors; 
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then he heals the wound like the others where one avoids a bowe, so that no vessel leaks that would nourish one of the corners; 
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because by those no evil comes, and if all the vessels come alive, then it is necessary to draw the corners of all the vessels;
