si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the vessel does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sciatic nerve
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The happening of this ramic is thus by the section that comes or where it is placed, or the extension above the belly in the part of the bowels, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either due to a blow or to the stretching of it, and these two manners of damage come from many causes: 
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or by percussion, or by jumping, or by falling, or by lifting a heavy weight, and by similar things.  
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is an extension due to a blow are that it happens in small parts, along a long time period, and does not come suddenly; 
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscess is even up to its point, because the blow quickens the intestines.  
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the abscess, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and there are various appearances of abscesses under the skin, and this for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the abscess.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it happens that the intestines are caught with the belt, and held in, and cause great pain to suffer to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, for which it behoves to avoid it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the treatment is that you instruct the patient to pull back the intestines with his hand inside the wound if he can enter it; 
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be sewn up above its neck between your hands, and raise its hips; 
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then is the hair on the above, and cut all of the skin of the scrotum from long.  
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the books of the waist pins according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that the eyes can issue out.   
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then skin the soft flesh that is below the skin of the scrotum, until the white flesh be uncovered from all parts;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your two index fingers in that which follows the scrotum, in that which is between the white flesh that is below the skin of the [testicle], and between the second flesh, and depart that which is behind the [testicle], and between the second flesh; 
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move with the right hand inside the hair of the scrotum, and have the white flesh on top to your left hand, and lift the [testicle] to all the flesh toward the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the minister to extend the arm upward, and untie those that are behind the ligament. 
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and seek at his two sides if he has any point of the intestine enveloped or white and hard there, and if you find none of these things, then put it into the belly below. 
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	Then take a needle or one that has the thick thread made of many threads, and put it into the rear part of the soft spot, which is after the skin of the buttocks. 
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads. 
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	Then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the soft spot, about which we have said that it is below the skin of the buttocks, with a strong bandage of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then envelope the hairs of the threads and bind them together in the form of two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except for an abscess. 
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put directly the linen according to the first linen long II must of that one, and after these II linens leave to the sifac which is below the heart of the loincloth the great one of a doe; 
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; 
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is below the skin of the loincloth, as long as the sinew, and the bow, as we have said before;  
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it in the wounds, and there administer the linen that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes is cauterized the white of the eye as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of the flowing of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the linen as long as it dries through it;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it delays in drying, so be raised from hot water, and put on what we have said, as long as it dries; 
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with other cures, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to do the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is joined to the trunk, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cutting above or lightly below. 
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	Then cut into it, and cure the abscess from those who work on it, until the vessels flow;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the groin, as we have said, and opens the flesh;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and let no parts of the bowels come out towards the genitals, and if any do come out, it is bad, and repair all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nevertheless if it remains too long at this point, the wound or abscess swells so that the intestine rises. 
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of the abscess which is swollen, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swollen with its parts and opened. 
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	And the cure for this is by cautery, as we have said before; 
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is cured by iron in this way:  
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	And that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then cut the area of the rupture swollen in breadth according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the abscess that is under the skin which you have cut, then take the iron and place it on the appearing area of the abscess;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and he presses at the forepart of the belly, then counts their two appearances of the sciatic upon the head of the thigh, and counts one and the other 
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extracts the head of the thigh, and does not cut of the sciatic nor extend any other thing, as I have made you know in the cure of the hernia of the bowels; 
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then cures it by the cure of wounds.  
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound as long as it is healing.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The wound is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times is softened the skin of the testicles in some men, because those things that are within are softened, and it is made to be seen;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie upon his back, and one cuts the skin which is softened upon the natural skin; 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then assembles the two lips with a stitch, and if you see, first stitch the superfluity of the softened skin to three stitches or four firmly; 
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then  bind between the ribs, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread. 
dou chastrement	through chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that chapterings are common in our law, and for that reason I would like to not speak of them in this book. 
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is necessary only for two manners:  
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	of which one is that the  mirrors know how to answer when they are asked, and also how to treat them; 
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need cauterization of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	Therefore I say that cauterization is done according to two manners: 
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by attraction, or by cutting.  
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the parts are softened and pliable; 
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	Then take hold of them with your hand, until they are put back in place and you no longer feel them.  
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the chastisement of the waist: 
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	It behooves you to hold the beast, and press the skin of the buttocks with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each side at the hip, when you have well scorched them.
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and I leave no point of the syfac and the subtle syfac which is on the vessels. 
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of chastisement is more effective than the one that is done by attraction, because in attraction perhaps nothing of the members remains, so the beast desires lust. 
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then care for the wound until it is healed.  
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as men: 
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one if between the two sexes it appears like the figure of a woman, or there is hair, and sometimes the urine comes out short.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it is on the pointed part also like a rod and they copulate.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the care of the man and woman is that you cut the joined parts all off, and treat them like other wounds;  
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	A wart is a carbuncle attached to the natural part, until it is too ugly to see.  
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	You should trim the excess of the wart to your hand or ones you have, and cut it lightly; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and don't pull too much from it, so that bleeding doesn’t come out, then the cure of other cures until it is healed; 
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and to another car that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and the stem, and by chance it happens, and is according to the resemblance of a cow, and for this they called it in ancient times "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the origin, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	 Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; 
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is natural by birth, or by accident through illness that has come to it; 
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or is caused by  a charmed joint or by subtle or strong sorcery, and is done in the thighs, or ribs, or underarms, or wherever; 
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevents conception, and childbirth, and possibly flowers from blooming;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	And the knowledge of these things is through the regard of the healer. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stroke is approaching near, if it pleases you to your two or to the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is from subtle sorcery, and it is close to the two books, hurry then, and do this:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two index fingers together, and the woman be on her back, legs spread; 
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then form the two books, as long as the subtle sorcery is strong, and until the numbness is over;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the spot, and lay the woman flat at home each day so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the suture is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stoppage is of flesh, then suspend it at the end and the top.  
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	And have the blood-thinning medicines, such as Acaice, dragon's blood, incense, and a mixture of egg yolk.  
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	Then administer a wide plank splint so that the wound cannot close; 
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	And thus it will be for a long time, and administer to him a tent of dry linen.  
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be cured with other dressings until he is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a boil comes in the flesh, it must be treated according to this manner, unless it is an inflamed abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the marsh, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened. 
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And we have said in the division the similarities of those [symptoms], and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the piles, when they are driven into the flesh, and they do not appear to the touch, unless by iron cure.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	Therefore it is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then take the hardened part with tongs and cut it at its roots, then powder on blood-restricting medicines such as Acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then put his feet to the air for an hour, then put it in cold water. 
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	And if blood comes out of the incision, make him sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and wine, and make a plaster on his back with it.  
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he withstands it, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that doesn't work, let him place suction cups on the back and breasts without hurting them; 
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply it there.  
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess heals, treat its place with ointment until it is healthy; 
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	And that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles the harsh herb, so it should be covered as I said in the previous section. 
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healthy. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancre and stony abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and more diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore I say in this treatment the hot abscess that comes on the arm, which is not like abscesses that swell. 
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not hasten to lance it, but let it mature until the pain is eased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats where he can recline, and support him on his back and bring his legs together towards the outside of the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then follow it towards the right side, and there administer the instrument with which one works the mouth of the marsh, so that afterwards comes the form; 
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you see administering this instrument, you first make the rake in order to know the depth of the marsh, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient;  
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the instrument does not injure him;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument above, and that he holds the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it with a soft hand, then it is necessary to cover it at the head, on the spatula left; 
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the wound is empty, then it is necessary that you put in the wound moistened pads in rose oil, or in green oil dry; 
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	And place the tent far from the wound to the edge of the flesh, and put outside on the flesh and on the linen blade clean moistened in water or malves are cooked;  
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure after II days of oiling preceding these, until it is healed. 
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	And no time lift the flesh and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then water or roots of lilies and arnica long are cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Then return to the oiling. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the mire, then it behooves you to guard against cauterizing with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	The profession is first to the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if it is when you see the woman pressing down, and desires to smell the air. 
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	therefore the child must hurry with force to straighten 
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	therefore know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and it is the issue under its head, and the second one with it. 
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, then it is appropriate to gently press on its belly so that the child issues forth quickly;  
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	because when it descends onto its head, then comes the second one with it, and is cleansed the womb of its superfluities by good purification; 
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.  
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	Because it comes sometimes on its feet, and comes forth with the body or shoulder, and the hands, or it comes onto its belly, or loin, and is converted by chance onto its neck, and by other bad figures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help her.  
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the infant comes out of its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth with great difficulty, and the strength of her is weak, then let them sit on a saddle, or let the women hold her.  
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and rose its nature of oil or fennel be cooked, and then put the bath between her thighs with the little spatula whose form is here: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	And split the perineum, and cut to its fingernail as far as the moisture that is inside it comes out;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and take the womb of the woman as long as the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to administer a clyster of fennel husk with sesame oil to the woman;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then let her take and sneeze from condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:  
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Then now extract the infant. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are dislocated, it is necessary that you reset them gently, bit by bit. 
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot go in, put the woman on the seat, and raise her feet up high; 
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then unseat the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the unseating;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot go in, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the knife which is placed before, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it bit by bit, until it is even; 
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then grasp its feet and extend them bit by bit.  
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If it jumps to the hips, then command to take hold of, and let it sneeze from its condition; 
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it shall jump, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, there he lightly treats.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come as we have, say that you take mustard seed of millet, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind everything in the mortar; 
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put it on the woman's area inside and cover this ointment, then have her sit in a bath of hot water until under the ribs; 
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened underneath, make her a collar of myrrh and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour; 
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on the seat, then have her sneeze and strain her mouth and nose, and gently pull on her belly, for the child will now jump.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, put the bailiff to his hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be careful on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and be lying on the bed; 
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	And bends his hands back and forth, and then takes the hands over the belly, and he pushes the cushions down, until she is positioned below. 
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child does not jump, then he takes his feet and moves them forcefully, then he lifts the belly upward, then he pushes with his hands. 
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and he shakes the child back and forth.  
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And instructs the woman to tighten herself until the child is delivered. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child who comes out with a hand wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to engineer bringing back the hand:  
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman rise and leave. 
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot leave, then have her lie on the bed and forcefully bend her legs;

et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and nurse the child according to natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to refrain from moving as long as the child breathes. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child upon his neck, and let his hands be spread, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the midwife grasps her hand, then turns it back and forth, and nurses gently.   
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, she places it on the natural muscle tissue of the high and oil it, as we have said, then commands her to move it back and forth. 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and command her to sneeze.  
et la fai esternuer.	and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner to all the back
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be this way throughout the whole secondine, she cuts the secondine with her fingernail until the moisture is emptied.  
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child strains on her face and neck, she cuts it from the bud, so that it is not held back, and kills the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then put the child inside, as long as you have put him as it is right, and command the woman that she does not touch herself at all times. 
adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore if it is lightly extracted.  
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are born many times, and never three or four. 
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	And this is not a strange thing, but it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if they are named at all. 
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they, being multiplied, and are divorced by the force which divides them, which is joined to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they come out as naturally as a single joint, as we have said.  
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out roughly, so treat them as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and make it quickly and lightly what it does.  
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is worth moving to health. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the marris I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its wise glory, and it is necessary that the bandage know all this, because perchance similar things happen. 
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if it is done according to what is necessary.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with hands;  
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or she has fear of death; 
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her shoulders inclined downward, and the legs raised; 
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister holds her by the sides, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not moved during the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oils with mulch of elder and fennel and flaxseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and mulches; 
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then put them in the woman's mouth gently, then press where she pushes out the contractions so they are comparable to these, and take heed if the child is appearing that it descends on its head; 
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if push the contractions in her eyes or her neck or her mouth or in her palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the contractions are at the legs, put them where the hip and the middle of the ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the needle in his right hand, and place the bend between the two of the left hand, and push it with all his hand lightly, and put the needle into any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing 
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the needle:  
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert against the other needle, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions be equal; 
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then make them equal by moving from one side and the other, so that it goes in smoothly, and let the needles be toothed to hold better, as this is the form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if any part remains, anoint the ball with some of his oil in that part, and push it in, and draw the other part;  
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains none of it, put this one-cine or higher place, and do so until it goes out completely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, it is necessary that you envelop it on the cloak, until it goes out completely. 
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then the cape at the joint of the sole or to the knife, and in this way you must do in the other hand, and as well with the feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's bone is thick and it is obstructed in the exit, or where it has a sharp point assembled, it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two, and making the head and extract the sharpness; 
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you turn it to the instrument that is called "almidach", because the form comes with the instruments or chapter that is after this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in the same way do so if the child has a large natural head; 
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps out and is strained by force, it should be split, until the moisture which is or worse comes out. 
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, cut it in pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture flows out. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on his feet, the traction is light, and the delivery at the mouth of the womb is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is in the belly or in the breast, it is necessary that you draw it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand. 
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and rub the belly or breast until the moisture inside comes out. 
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are obstructed and the head remains, put your hand in the mouth of the vagina and pull it until the mouth of the vagina.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he puts it back in one place or the other, and the bone is healed. 
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the abscess is tightened because of the heat cauterization that has come, it does not need to be worked on, but instead one must administer moist and fatty things. 
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administer poultices, and sicca in softened and moisturizing water.   
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its ribs, and you can put it straight, administer those things we have said in a living child; 
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do this, then the bone will be healed in pieces, and nothing of the secondary (fragment) shall be left. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, administer those things we have said in abscesses that come in the mouth;  
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding occurs, it is put in restraining water, and other treatments are administered. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time there came an abscess in the swelling, and it inflamed so much that it opened and began to great purulence.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long time, and could not solder the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a strong plaster on it, and after some days one bone protruded, and after some other days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was much amazed because this one whose belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I washed the wound, and with my hands I moved the bones, until the woman was in a better state; 
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and treated the woman for a long time thus, and so it came to pass that she had a little bit of swelling from there.  
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I haven't recorded this chapter for anything else than because when the masters find a strange thing, that they may know how to help.  
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the bone to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here after comes the form of the pressure, which one has in the books; 
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to II turns as II joints of II limbs. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nonetheless, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be 1/2 inch wide, and the margin of the trees it must, and long one palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and among the two limbs be two joints of this same fist, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or an inch more; 
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the mare for opening when one turns the two horns.  
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pliers;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two joints with two adjustments, as you see, half a palm long, and two widths wide; 
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see to open the mare with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, her feet dangling and legs open, then put the two adjustments together in the mare, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips; 
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then work your hand on all the instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the jaws, as long as the bait does what it wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all surmounted, and multiply their likenesses.  
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	And when the mirrors have appeared to them, so much is more haste in the work, and higher for men for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not disdain the instrument, so long as it is well prepared for it its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze of condition, and restrain your hands to her mouth and nose; 
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps for this, well is.  
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this is not the case, then take an iron pot, and make a perforated cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the jaws, such as calamine, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	All these herbs, or none of them, be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; 
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a chain or a perforated piece in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the patient, and steam it until the vapor comes from within the patient's mouth; 
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make him sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second bone leaps violently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment and is not better, as we command the midwife to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in the mucus of a leek, and then put it into the patient's orifice, and  rub it with the second finger; 
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she will have found it, she grasps and extends it little by little straight ahead so that the patient's mouth does not close during the extraction; 
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but then you must move it gently to the right and to the left, and then pull; 
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and unties itself. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the nose is blocked, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; 
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not relieved by all that we have said, then be careful that you do not use the milk;  
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the nose, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then enema with ointment tetra-pharmacon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if she will endure and put it back, and come forward;  
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nonetheless, when she endures, then a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and the patient becomes pale.   
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Therefore it is necessary fumigation suitable to that:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	none of the ancients have proven fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument for which one fumigates the woman to restrain the flowers and the womb is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And is to see similar to a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders broad over the fire. 
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let be the fumigation over the coals, and the tar until it is roasted, and begin again another.  
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped by subtle stitches. 
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, it befits the midwife to pierce that stitch at its due place, and do not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guard the thread so that she does not touch it. 
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on linen moistened in wine and oil, then the ointment care until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will set right again, then put in a piece of splint and leave the limb for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes this stupefaction comes from a wound or an abscess. 
si covient coper celui soudement:	If it is necessary to cover that boil:  
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it is cured, as we have said of the plantain cautery. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are knotted, and thicker than those that come from near the foundation of outside, or in the space between the two parts, whether it is one fistula or more. 
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	And when that knotting is old, it works, and still moisture from within brings out white or thin boils, and sometimes these fistulas are opened. 
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by those who feel them or have emission or venting when the patient has a bowel movement and perhaps one bursts out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; 
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach up to the hip joint, and up to the knee.  
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing to the base, and not piercing. 
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And that you put your middle finger or foundation, and put a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has torticollis, put in a tent of fine lead, or horse hair, until you feel the tent or hair on your finger. 
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of pus nor wind nor worm as we have said:  
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not pierce. 
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure.  
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the channel of urine, if it leaks urine, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the junction of the hip, then the thread comes up to that place; 
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the invention of pain within, then it is that it is there bowed, and there is no use for medicine or treatment by ointment;  
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except for labor, and the vanity of foolish tricks that intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one which is not persistent and is not ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on their back; 
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his hips, and has his thighs inclined to his belly;  
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then set a tent of lead, or of plummet if there is torsion, as long as you know where the tent comes from. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it around the base, then it is fitting that you put your index finger on it, if thus you feel that the tent has pierced. 
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and be uncovered where you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then know that it is pierced; 
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not travel at all one cannot heal it.  
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said anyway one can well heal none, but this happens little; 
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that one makes it, is if one cauterizes the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; 
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	And the end brings all heat into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation. 
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred hairs are burned, which resemble the feather of an eye; 
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moist bandages smeared with butter, as long as those charred hairs are gone, then cure it with an ointment that hardens and heals. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If so, he is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, otherwise cannot be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters and does not reach the bottom which is the foundation, and there is between your bottom and the tent a thick covering of char or sebac, and you see the fistula following this covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then cauterize after, as long as it reaches the top of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and will be delivered the tent, and will fall. 
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then seize those charlatans who seem like a bird's feather, and leave none remaining.  
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound pains, and comes between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery assembles two good things: 
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of those attached charlatans, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; 
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of tents soaked in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound lies bowed, and if the charlatan is burned in the bowed; 
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound of swollen onions with enduring hard char, and they are dry medicines.  
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is reset, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the foundation, and is distant from the body, put your finger on it or its base, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between it there is the cloth or the syfac or charlatan, or if he is near to piercing, then there is only a way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three ways: 
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put bandages on it and treat it as before. 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and don't let it become too bad, that you cut the foundation holding it, and come the excretions by its willing sense; 
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;  
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound then that it is cut from its foundation, or by bandage or by another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the festered flesh in the wound, as much as you can; 
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and leave the fistula in the part outside the foundation;  
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And no times are fistulas according to this manner:  
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or against the foundation near the skin above, so take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts the thread wrong in it, and puts the tent at all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that one pierced, just as you put your finger or foundation; 
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and let it for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no time, until the threads have gripped those parts that are between two, and hold tight;  
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed and sound. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in every way that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to make the lace for covering if they are so embroiled, and then care for it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula spine from which one makes the fistula is very often one part and trenches;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other part no, because of which one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here; 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: 
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are within the foundation, as well as grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, blood comes out, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation. 
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are outside have little moisture, and in short, they come out with a little bit of clear water or a little blood, and have the color of the body; 
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, it is that you command the patient to stretch so they can lie in rooms, as long as the foundation is sore and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hasten, and can hold it with pliers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; 
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the clamp cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them to the drapery or cotton, or a piece of felt. 
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them with your two hands, then cut them, and powder above any hot powders that are in their place of cautery. 
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed.  
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the base cannot come out, then enema the patient with a harsh and sharp enema to wash what is in the base so that it can come out clearly. 
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient endures well, and if the threads are further from the base, then the cure is light.  
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and if you pick them with your finger or pliers and cut them, then cure them as we have said until they are healed, and that he fears the incision by iron.  
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner:  
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce through from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so let them be wide; 
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tighten the thread firmly, then remove the needle, and do this for all the others, leaving one open to drain the excess blood; 
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on top of the foundation a soft cloth in rose oil or in cerate, and put it on top of the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; 
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave him until they heal, and when they are healed, cure them with ointment and other cures, until he is cured. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of fluids in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not useful.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you scrape to the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not let it become moist;  
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat until it is healed as it should; 
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scabbed over. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat until it is healed.  
dou fremit	from trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A forence is a small appearance of fault before the body, and goes much in depth. 
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the cold, and one feels it also like death from chill, and comes in the whole body, and more to the hands than any other place.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a feather of goose, or a feather of vulture strong, and put that feather on the chill, until the circles paint the chill all around.  
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand on the whole feather until you scrape all around the chill, and put it in depth, and scrape the chill from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this, do as follows of a hook of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not perceive, for to hold onto the two, and squeeze.  
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see it, cauterize the flesh, like it is before in the chapter of cautery. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	At times one makes a clyster of silver or archate, or lead melted or maillet;  
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and at times one makes of these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.   
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are treated in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema tube small and great is this above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	And if there is a separation or the belly is tied, like you see, and the shoulder blade is pierced inside; 
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and has on one of the ribs two pierced, and in the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly where one puts medicines of an animal bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and has between each hole a measure of space, then put in these holes one strong thread of spun wool twisted into X or intertwined, and assemble the belly like it is a kid; 
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	And when the medicine is inside, if the ligature is at the instrument in front of a strong thread, then enema. 
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And this is the form of the circle:
