Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and ointment the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently.  
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the minister squeezes it with his two hands together, until it is all expelled, then withdraws the enema, and raises the patient’s legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to flow out, then hold as much as you can.  
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if he sleeps all night straight through, it is of greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him with a laxative for a stomach ailment, and the medicine quickly departs, so let it return until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or an abscess, then let the enema be as subtle as for a child.  
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the clyster subtle with which the skin is strained 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in the previous section the cure of wounds;  
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you about the cures of hands and medicines, according to their completion. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from that which they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and cuts of sword and knife, or spear or dart or arrow, or similar things; 
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar members;  
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you take care it is from blows of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt heavily of an abscess hot: 
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it immediately heals of the head, even if a little blood comes from the wound, and the bleeding is on the contrary side of the injured part; 
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient's intake of wine and heavy meats.  
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his meat be lessened, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; 
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes from it, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in wine poultice; 
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not dryed by the air, powder, which I will say a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has dried, put on some ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then bring them together by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a bit, cut it. 
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then heal the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotting skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut out all the rot, and throw it away, then heal it. 
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without a cautery, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it displaced, tie it with a thread. 
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, then cauterize it.  
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: 
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put in this powder which unites as if the iron had melted it.  
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is: 
pren encens une partie;	Take frankincense one part; 
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;  
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Heat live III parts, and powder finely, and apply to the wound, and restrain it firmly, until it closes well and joins with all its blood; 
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then cover it well, and let it remain unbandaged, if it does not swell; 
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one removes the medicine only when it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with caulks alone, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has broken open the wound, even in this state, do not put this powder on it; 
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digested ointment or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it heals well; 
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pincers; 
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes at the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it to heal, and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the nerve and causes it to retreat. 
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation so is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be warm, such as  calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and calcined wash also in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch and bind with bandages, then treat until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is raised and full of pus, then pierce or lower them; 
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes out, then sever it, and tie it, and cauterize it if it is necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is kept, because the flesh goes, so sew the heart above the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural form. 
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then restrain it well, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointment dressings until it is healed. 
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then so desire it;  
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, treat them as much as you can, and what you cannot have, leave it until the wound rotts, and be cleansed and align the opening. 
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, put the powder on it that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, so treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or a knife and the wound is deep, see if from the wound there is windiness as the patient complains.  
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any of the powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it up to keep the blood from flowing too deeply, and returning to the heart, and killing the patient.  
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I put attractive ointment, and bind it two times a day; 
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, put in the wound old cotton to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;  
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there come not any spasm, nor bad shaking of heart nor straining of arm; 
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, then you know that the wound is saved.   
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal it then with bandages and other dressings, as long as it be healed; 
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and opens, then you know that there is a fistula.  
si la cure si com on doit.	then treat it as one must.   
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is of incision of sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, treat it as above.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, sew 
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, so close the wound, and bring out the fragments if they are loose; 
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, leave the wound to rot, it will lighten the extractions;  
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other members, the judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound, sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines come out, because of which the intrusion of others; 
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because of which one puts back the intestines in, if not done immediately after.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Because the intestines swell at once when they feel the cold, they return more to points, and for this reason the middle wound hurts more, because of this one resets the intestines to their place like the others II. 
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is in IV manners:  
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the other sutures of other wounds of the body and two other special sutures are common to other wounds; 
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine has come out, and it is a matter of putting things back, this is by one of the two manners: 
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either for the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.  
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: 
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Soak a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you cook in hot water with saffron and cypress and spice, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed;  
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never make this wine restraining, and it moves only that little to deflate. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with lukewarm water or ale and herbs are cooked, because by this it is aligned the entrance to little things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument by which hemorrhoids are cut; 
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first cure is to be made smaller than the incision, that none of it should be cut without great necessity; 
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting: 
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it is cut inside in the curve and outside not, and see here the form:  
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails protrude, you put them back in their natural form in their proper place, if you are able, because it is worth moving.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; 
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, put the head and the chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention so that the sunken part is higher than the other; 
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and small wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Small wounds put what you have seen, then hold in your hands the minister pitiful that holds all the rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; 
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of suturing, and it is that you pierce an needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound one doe of space, and there put a needle where there is the good strong thread; 
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the sinew, which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the two heads of the sinew the four together.  
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then the strain of a double thread around the needle of two parts, then assemble the two ends of the wound evenly, and then leave one doe of space, and there put another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then the tie of the thread as you have done with the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need of needles, until the whole wound is restrained. 
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium, between fine and thick, for the fine needles pierce all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: 
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For this reason, they should be medium.  
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And it is not fitting to push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the stitching. 
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then trim the tips of the needles so they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put tents or drapes on the wounds to keep them covered, and let them stay until the wound is stitched. 
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because one or two needles suffice.  
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitching is common, and it is that you assemble the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh together with one needle to which a strong medium thread is attached.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you will have pierced these bones all four together, then reset the needle to the part where you began, in the manner in which one sews drabs. 
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each suture the thickness of a man's finger; 
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This suture seven the man, and I sewed a wound that one man had in his belly, which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it was two palms wide of intestines, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestines after they had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound was healed up to XV days, and I treated him, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not heal him with ointment, because I was in the place where one could not find any, nor any medicines; 
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put half a pound of cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until he was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways to sew:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and push it from the outer part to the inner one. 
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the heart of right in a straight line, lay the head above the site where you pushed the needle in, and make it pierce from the other side from the inner to the outer. 
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furrier does furs, and that you leave one side of the site open, and take it up from the other, until the stitch is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of stitching, that the Galens describes properly, is like when any one assembles the two parts together naturally, and apply one head of the site to the other head, in such a way: 
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stick a needle or head of the mirror close, and make it pierce that point only, and leave the two heads of the site.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inside one, like the two shoulders.  
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then make it pierce both from the outer part to the inside one, in two other shoulders of the mirror that are on the other side.  
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most common and usual manner of sewing. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	The Gauls say this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the sewing is more grievous than the other parts of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: 
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the fire has moved it, so put back the intestine and the skin; 
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder containing charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, put on any ointment that is available, as long as the wound heals; 
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and stitch the thread, and be joined the flesh, and the membrane; 
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; 
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicine in more cases than the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound does not make community with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten a linen cloth lightly in oil of tempered heat, or rose oil, and put it around the joints, and under the buttocks. 
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or rot in the belly, and this happens many times, then give enemas of black wine, and also if the putrefaction comes up to the intestine. 
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called «jeun» cannot heal when it is ravaged, and this is because of the planting of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps out of the wound, put it back inside as well as the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has become worm or black, it is necessary that you tie the place which is black, so that no blood comes out, because there are veins and arteries there. 
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then take what is between the bones, and put the two heads during from beneath the wound all the way out to align the extraction when the bone falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, because I have seen that some man was pierced through the belly by a spear. 
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and through it passed feces and flatulence. 
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him according to what I could, and did not cease until it was healed, and the edges were closed. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closed, I doubted that the patient would have badly in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better disposition, and ate and drank. 
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And certain experimenters say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such manner: 
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take fresh cloths of large tests, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the cloth has covered the opening, place it above the two edges so that it strains its mouth shut; 
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then you cover the head, and it stays so that it cannot be untied, then place the other cloth after in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed; 
et cout la plaie.	And sew the wound.  
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This chief is done in the intestine and no harm comes to the patient, and it can be tied with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such manner: 
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the thread of this intestine that is quite clean, and then tie it to the end of this fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine with it, and wind it into the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching of fragments is not other than according to the way of hope and promise; 
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the great internal veins, there is nothing but subtlety 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is closed and inward curved.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the truth a knotted and hard and white thing, where one does not feel pain, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird; 
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear and narrow, and other times thick; 
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times enough;  
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is nothing other than by one of the IX causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or for his wickedness; 
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because he has hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to be born.  
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or he has too much swelling; 
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wounds are rotting, and the matter is of bad quality.   
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for the cure;  
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is tardy for digestion, and slow for health, and swollen by nature;  
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones. 
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.  
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is therefore necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body; 
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the bladder, or intestine, or kidney, or any of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet. 
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar ones.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to see it known, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, if it wishes; 
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is crooked, then make a search of a subtle tent of lead, because lead bends itself around the crookedness; 
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by tents, then have it clstered through one of the openings, because moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it;  
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then carefully with your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and are bruised in place, and ask the patient well of the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and where he feels it;  
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then act according to what I have told you, and remove the foreign matter and corrupted flesh that are within; 
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then care for it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep from right place, then it is necessary that you cut into it as deep as you can, then put moist bandages in medicinal ointment, and push them to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is at the bottom; 
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointment for healing fresh flesh, until it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it away. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not strike or affect principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then  remove it as much as the corruption is gone, then cure with healing things for flesh until it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and returns bowed as before, know that you have not gone all the way: 
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	then expose and go as far as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is good. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not so, know that the corruption is too deep in part, that you cannot come to it.  
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is nothing else but to leave it to nature; 
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it out with tweezers, if you extract it with a tool suitable for this, and if there are many bones, you draw them all, do not leave even one. 
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture makes it difficult for you, and there is no error or fear, cut through both moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.   
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, place on the wound something preventing rot, and leave until the flesh around the bones is rotten, and then the bones will come out more easily.  
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, like from the leg or thigh, you resect only as much of the corruption as the blackness has been removed completely, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a large part of corruption, and it comes to near the bone. 
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	Then it must be scraped and covered all the way to the corruption, and then it must be cured until it is healed. 
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take it as an example and help with your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, until the materials came to the leg, and became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause for opening.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the physicians, through their folly, opened too much so that the abscess opened, and they corrupted a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there came a lot of pus that all flowed out and moist from within the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many a man was cared for for two years, and there was no sage in the art of hands, until I came to be called upon him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what ran out through the wounds;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the youth became red at the joints, and had a citron color.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I then hastened, and dug into one of the wounds until I discovered a portion of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came as far as the inner bone;  
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed that which appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except that which I removed;  
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not heal it;   
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuing corruption in the bone, and I treated it, and then I set the bone, and I prepared to solder the place.  
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could not do more than I joined together around a palm of the bone, and the traitor was pulled to its whole size, then I restored it with medicines. 
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was healed and joined immediately, and it was not necessary to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the blood evacuation often happened, but it was cured entirely, and in the place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was in good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary at all, neither to going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be treated in this manner: 
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take linen and tie it to the head of the bone that is open, and command anyone who stretches it upward.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another link of linen bigger than the first one, and tie it on the flesh which is above the bone, and hold the head so that you pull the corrupted flesh down below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see should be, so that the skin does not bleed from the flesh; 
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a piece of wood or a board below the bone to move and cover the corrupted flesh;  
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it should be as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and should be still another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open well, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely; 
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put the piece of wood below, and then move it from one part to the other the corruption, and be the suture of the long side of the corruption the point, as we have said; 
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and bone where it contains from the other side.  
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else to cut; 
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or the finger of the foot, it is a very serious thing, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you. 
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And purify it in every way that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not cause you contrary.  
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that the cutting instrument and the threads for covering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason it is necessary to equip each type of work with its instrument. 
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases. 
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you consider the instrument which you need according to what is appropriate.  
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can dislocate either inward or outward; 
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the dislocation comes from, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or from the malice, which is greater, of the defect of the limb; 
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it has been burned by fire, and after the blackness, then that corrosion from limb to limb goes, and takes hold of the whole body. 
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hurry to cover it, and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, like a sea scorpion and viper and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give him any space to come until the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes until the hand, then cover it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come until the arm. 
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes to the arm, then cover it with the knife;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no worth administering further remedies than the quantity of its virtue. 
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And so do all this when the corrosion comes or foot.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes in the first joint, then cover it after the other joint. 
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes to a foot, cover the whole foot.  
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends to the leg, cut at the knee joint.  
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die; 
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister on one of the ties below, and others ministers the other tie above, and you sever the flesh that is between the two ties to a spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered; 
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or sew, and put on each side the draping of linen, so that the sewing does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess clothes. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the place thoroughly, or you put on some restraining powders. 
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed. 
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to the man in his foot:  
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackening that resembled fire burns, and this corrosion first came in his instep, until it encompassed the whole foot. 
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed.  
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And long afterwards the corrosion returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things  receptive after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion. 
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he urged me to cover his hand, and I refused because I had hope of containing the matter.  
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and doubt also if he cuts his hand, that he may not die because the virtue of the man was weak.  
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired of all, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed. 
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not this recounted outside of that which one does otherwise, if one has need.  
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in its fleshy place, and remains so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; 
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and out leaps the pus, and remains in its place as a vessel. 
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin which is above it is as fine as a delicate tapestry, and does not run until to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called 'sound,' and is not called 'fistula'; 
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it comes to the bone making a path, it is called “fistula”; 
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin there is that you cut that skin all around, and also when it is thinned, like a cloth; 
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not let it for its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have faith that the skin will harden, and the corruption is not in its path, and the skin is thick of flesh, then treat it with a clyster like this: 
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the breasts are large, and the bosom that is in it is of foul odor, then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made like this: 
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take ails, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of those according to your need, and make them sharp and in honey, and in a clyster the breast, and restrain the opening; 
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.  
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breasts are drained and the pain is removed. 
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at no time is a clyster of water and ashes used when this medicine is present, and that you take ashes from a vine stick, and pour water on top, then let it drain, and in a clyster, until you know that the breasts are well drained. 
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water and ashes, then clyster them with water and honey or where there is a piece of litharge ground; 
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you cleanse it with honey and sweet wine, so that the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes it dry. 
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well purified, then you will make a clyster of those which cause flesh to be born in it, and that you take plaster diaphinit, and do it with rose oil and wine; 
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you will make a clyster of certain medicines and ointments, about which I have spoken of the properties or treatment of ointments; 
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the breast is small, and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter it, then widen it with an iron a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basil oil, as long as it is widened; 
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then you sew it and leave only as much space as the clyster can enter, and if the opening that gives birth to the bowel is above, then cover or lower the level where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the stomach is in full form, there does not let flesh enter. 
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then arrange it in such a manner that the stomach descends to its lowest point because when the stomach is full, there does not let flesh enter and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then arrange it in such a manner: 
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the stomach descends gently downward, and leave nothing of the stomach behind.  
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidated medicines to put upon the groin, and be over the linen cloth that covers the whole groin.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover as forces the spot of the groin more wide than the first one, then be ointment under the other cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound of the groin to align the stomach, and do not remove the large cloth outside except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is through the breast wound, bone often to remove the bowel, and know those that run from the bowel, if it's venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; 
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take ward if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or no, and when your medicine has been in such a manner extended and you see the nature that jumps on the breast wound, so you know that the breasts are already healed, and approaching health;  
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, so change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.  
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed ingestible after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venoms come after a long time, if it does not trouble you of health, for the health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is delayed, and those who do the opposite; 
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the indigested bowel jumps from the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not healing; 
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the breast is slow to heal and is swollen, so apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, like diaphinit ointment, because it contains a large part of vitriol, and this is the last remedy;  
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; 
puis le confit et en use;	Then confit it and use it;  
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And the same way, make honey cooked with rose petals, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take frankincense, aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then glue it to the cloth, and place it over the breast, and sometimes administer a long stalk of aristolochia, and roots of celestial lilies, which is also like flour made from chickpeas and wormwood;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And in the use of simples or of composites: 
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them, and make a powder, and put on top the honey that I said, and use it.  
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the wound is prolonged and is not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has entered deep, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs. 
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of a fistula, as we have said before.  
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A panaritium is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps arises in other places. 
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is neglected and one does not take care of it, then an abscess comes, and it corrodes and throws out a boil until it corrodes the root of the nail, and perhaps the whole thing.  
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corrosion to the bone, as much as it comes painful pain, and is the shoulder of two large, and is the color fluxed. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity which is left of the wound, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the joint is healthy; 
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the joint presses the flesh in and it begins to prick and swell, then it is necessary that you put the cautery under the joint so that it does not prick the flesh, and thrust it upward, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and place on the remaining flesh medicines ardent and corrosive to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and treat it further, because as much as the bone is corrupted it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the two do corrupt, then cut it in one as we have said before, then care for it until it is healed 
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and swollen, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first.  
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the joint with a sharp spatula by cutting across above, and guard that the cut does not come until the flesh which is below the joint, because the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top which soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance there is some where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born in any place of the two does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cut of he who is fleshy is light, in this manner: 
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure:  
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold him to cut. 
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In someone who is born or must have the afterbirth removed, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh around until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The soldering that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by soldering of wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you cut that suture so that it may heal according to its natural forms;  
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not fuse together; 
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of thin lead until the ligaments are fused, as it is fitting.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a joint comes together with its palm, so bind it as is fitting.
des vils	of the evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are thick envelopes full of melancholic superfluities that come into many members of the body; 
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and there are more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry than in others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It therefore becomes necessary for you to administer to him once purging of colocynth, then a potion from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure of iron is according to II manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is to cut them and draw out the black blood; 
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other manner is that you raise the vein, and treat it with all force. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is according to this manner:  
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First put the leg in hot water very strongly, until the swelling is diminished, then bind the leg of the patient from above the hip to below the knee; 
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in its place, whether in I or II or III, with a wide incision, then elevate and treat with force drawing out the black blood from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the disease allow.   
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it up, and command him to stay with black-legged meat; 
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, and harm the patient.   
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The elevation of the limb follows this manner: 
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell. 
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bathing water, heat it over the fire, and then apply the hot water to the vein of the long bone in the thigh or at the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then open the skin with the scalpel, and scrape the vein on each side until it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; 
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then pull the root down until it is elevated from the skin, and then cut it lightly with the scalpel, and then put it in another place above III joints.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it at the base, as you have done, and place it on another incision, as you did first. 
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another opening, or more if you need it, then lift it, and cut to the double of the foot, then thread and lift up to the second incision. 
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it piece by piece, until it is completely out, then cut it. 
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot thread and lift it, then put a needle into the entire strong double thread, and tie and thread it, and put it below the base, and turn your hand from one side and the other, until it comes out.
