et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then one cannot thread or lift it, and it brings much trouble to the patient. 
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it completely, put on the wound a cloth moistened with wine and rose oil; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.  
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the skin is constricted and twisted and covered together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then it is necessary that you cut it jaggedly, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which you cut the skin is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut into the vein; 
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a thick curve, because if it were thin, it would cut into the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where there do not grow herbs nor trees, and in land where it has no moisture; 
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And by chance, it is born in other places than the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes from within the body, snakes and worms, between the skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes the color, and begins the vein to go forth as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder is opened, it is necessary that you wrap around one piece of plank from one and a half to two fingers, and tie it, and leave the plank on the leg, and every time that there is pain on the outside, wrap around the plank, and tie it. 
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out.  
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and brings an abscess and rot there, and a bad illness.  
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, for that reason, it is necessary that it be treated piece by piece until the top, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein when it is treated with the palms of length, or of ten, and one man came to me, whose it went out for ten palms long, and when you cut it, it brings out the root or pierced, and pierces it to the bottom, so that all comes out; 
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And be emptied the matter which is within, and administer at the place medicines preventing corruption any day, then the cure as with the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes in this vein many pains, and even when it opens at the joint of the foot, or of the foot, and there comes much blood, and from which it jumps out;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure therefore as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land “disease of the ox”, because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the whole body rising and falling, and one feels it well at the alert of limb in limb, until they reach the skin where it goes, and jumps out; 
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the rotting of some humors, such as those that come from worms and lice and roundworms in the belly 
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malignancy, because when it goes through the body and goes up to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; 
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.  
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and milked, then it can only be driven away when it goes: 
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong linen tightly, then cut above it and drive it out, and if it goes back into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; 
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, then restrain under it the eyebrow forming, then cut above, and the path be cured. 
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the patient with purification of body and medicines soluble for the corrupted humors, and beware of rotten meats. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This malady is called in our land 'vakirir', and is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; 
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I see what I tell you.  
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; 
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I looked after, and I saw it rise also as a worm to the shoulder, more quickly than anything, as if live silver when it moves from place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from that place, and it goes into the shoulder, and then a little after it spreads throughout the body, until it comes to the other arm.  
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that she was turning back around her body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this sickness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted to move the pain from that place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman. 
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought to myself that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins uncovered, and for this reason appeared that constraint of windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate and have moist bodies and veins covered.  
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, so tie above and below gently, and then cut on top until that constraint of windiness has issued forth. 
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;  
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with those who expel wind ailments, such as fetid pills and wormwood pills, and similar ones. 
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and hairy, and smooth;  
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have two angles, and those that have tongues, and those that have parts; 
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that fall in any member, they fall in two ways;   
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in principal members such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterward, appears to you: 
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Therefore it is necessary for you to be careful with the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in many cases. 
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely extracted, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the skull which is above the brain, is when there is clouding and numbness and dizziness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of mucus; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps this with pain from the nostrils or ears; 
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps he loses his speech and voice;  
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound white moisture resembling pus, and also leaps as if burning of flesh; 
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the wound, and treat the arrow if it is not already out.  
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or rests in the body is that it is near the left breastbone, and it feels as if it were lodged in something hard, not hollow. 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: 
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death is approaching.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves the common is that without pains of foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the sick turns color, and sighs high and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the ribs, it is near the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and throws great pain and great sorrow and sighing; 
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and moves all the limbs from the shoulders.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes or stomach, by adventure there leaps out from the wound some thing of undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls or into the belly, and in no place of bone through the gut, there is no hope for healing, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain. 
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.  
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder joint and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and the seeming members, are safe according to more disposals.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that reason that you do the same thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into the root of his nose. 
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and it came out on the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without feeling anything.  
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in another case, an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye below the eyebrow, and the arrow was embedded, and I could only reach the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, to all the iron light without ears; 
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The fellow was healed, and no bad accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was Arabic with ears; 
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barbs, and I carefully extracted it as much as I could, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And treat an arrow to a man, who it was in his chest or belly, and thought he would die.  
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that he had passed XXX days, so he did not change his condition. 
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and I enclosed it, and I pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if a man has an arrow that fell in his back, and the wound is closed on top; 
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow stays inside him, and does not change his natural dispositions, nor does he feel any inconvenience in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if another man has an arrow that fell in his face, and the wound is closed; 
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and stays like that without suffering much pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And they pulled out an arrow from the prince's man, who had it lodged in his neck, and was slightly leaning to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	And the arrow was completely hidden. 
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to care after it had fallen three days.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined it thoroughly with a fine touch, and felt nothing of it; 
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it did not feel any sharpness or pain below its right ear.  
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed above its location a poultice atractive and digestive, because its skin did not swell; 
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the skin around the arrow appeared.  
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the poultice for a few days, and it closed the wound immediately, and the patient remained thus for a long time until he felt the arrow one day within his nose; 
et il le me dist.	and he told me this.  
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound an acrid corrosive medicine for a few days until it was open, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which was becoming loose at that place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I adjusted in the opening of the wound with this medicine sharp, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; 
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And pierced well the ends during IIII months, and then enlarged the wound that I put in forceps, and my pliers on one side and the other, and it cannot come out; 
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I did not cease to subtly tinker and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day forceps well made, according to those whose form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I pulled it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:  
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I therefore restored it, and the wound was soldered, and the patient was healed entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on those which I do not say, because the books cannot comprehend everything. 
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare on very little thing, and on what is present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to the descent of strange things that happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows are not from the members where they are fixed further than according to two manners: 
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part; 
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which is further by the place where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and never further now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go further, let it remain as long as the flesh is porous inward, and let the exit be open;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot issue, let it remain thus for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and therefore she jumps, and if she does not jump, then it pierces around to the whole forest subtle, until the lews around are enlarged, and then the treat.  
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient:  
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if do not treat it, but leave it as long as it is equal after some days, because if the arrow comes as far as the syfac, then it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed further than in the bone only, and does not come up to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then the engine of the milking.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot be pulled out further, then you administer tarriers around, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure the place until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned in its place in the body and one cannot see it, then one looks for it with all their strength.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, treat it with any suitable instrument; 
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the depth of the wound, and the great depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nor nerve, nor vein, then make a cut as long as the wound is large; 
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, then remove the flesh that is stuck on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can draw it out; 
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful that you do not break the arrow, that you may draw it out more easily.   
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, lay it until the place is softened, then treat it, because extraction hurts.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard against cutting the nerve and the vein, and put everything as much as you can to draw out the arrow safely, whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; 
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place if one sees or feels it apparently: 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then, as much as the pliers can take hold, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it leaps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is left in, pull out the whole shaft; 
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer force, then administer the instrument so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push forward, and if the arrow is stuck, put an instrument with a pointed tip into it to ease extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is surrounded, it behooves you to cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the chest or abdomen or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it up, then cut into it. 
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch up the wound, if it is necessary. 
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.   
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of an eye, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:  
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the hair is also like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the arrow, as it is in form.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers to insert and to know if it is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins that are used for healing there are thirty-one, because of which it has or head sixteen, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two behind the ears, which are called the two "herbaches"; 
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples appear 
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspirates";  
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead 
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the neck 
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck 
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";  
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly draws blood in each arm: 
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it runs along the outer side of the arm, and the common people call it "the vein in the arm";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the vein is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart";  
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilica is found along the right rib, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the furrow, and it is the one from which one draws blood, which opens visibly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the cephalic vein is the vein that is between the ring finger and little finger, and it has two branches;  
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: 
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the pouch on the left rib, and the second is called saphenous which is at the ankle on the right rib;  
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nerves", which is in the ankle of the other side. 
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are III veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The sap of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs, and headaches;  
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the sap, as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; 
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a strip, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then place them [the sap] on your thumb, and where you feel the pulse below your thumb, make it flow; 
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and put it under the vein to the bone, then lift your hand on all the vein above, and cut both the skin and the vein well two fingers deep, and make blood flow as much as you see; 
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and restrain it until it is healed; 
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for old migraine, and sore eyes, and habitual ophthalmia, and to sharp pains in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the draining are as I say: 
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient restrains his neck, so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulses below his back, and then directs the incision; 
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lifts the key above the vein on his right index finger, and puts the lancet below it, and raises the vein upward, and cuts it, just as you have done with the other veins, and make a drawing of blood according to your need; 
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then unbind the patient, and put your hand upon the vein for one hour, then put on cotton; 
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then let it form a knot, and leave it until it is healed;  
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of this and their treatment and their extraction, how the book begins. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for diseases of the face ancients, and migraine, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears. 
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor," whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point upon the vein, and hold with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see. 
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again open with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it does not behoove that the flames are too thick; 
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the healing should be across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.  
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The incision of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and to the chin, and to the redness, and to the pupil in the eye, and to diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the qualities of their incision are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with a bandage, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then make the incision, and let it be the incision through the middle, one part long of the flame one part wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks. 
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a correction of the blood, as much as you need, and then place it on cotton, and tie it well.  
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The bloodletting of the vein of the nose is good for fevers, and for headaches, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes on the face, even when it is old. 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose with your left hand, and takes the subtle long flame, and places it halfway between the two nostrils, because the vein doesn't open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And don't let it go too deep in there, and make a correction of the blood according to your need, then tie it overnight because it is very quickly restored. 
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the II winds helps in the treatment of the ailment, and the beginning of melancholy, and many illnesses, and epilepsy, and corrosion, and herpes, and scabies. 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the blood are that the patient strains his neck under both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on the seat, then cuts open the vein long a little widely, then draws out the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary. 
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the other part in the other vein, then untie the linen, and tighten both veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave him until morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins of the lips above helps in the ulcer in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and in toothaches and pain
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the bloodletting are to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; 
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: 
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, so cut the largest of each side, and also make of the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the cephalic bloodletting, and it is to the stricture of the throat, and to diseases of the eye, and to diseases of the mouth; 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the vein are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks down on each side a black vein: 
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then one and the other, and do not pierce too deep into them, for below are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm which are commonly bled are drained according to two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they prick at the whole flame, morning wide, or olive subtle as you cut sharp, and it is called “ansel”; 
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and the thickness of the veins.   
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame martin is very renowned, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the veins that are swollen plains of gross blood apparent, and which contain gross and turbid blood; 
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive cut:  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and at the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly. 
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it befits the physician to treat wisely, and to avoid the artery which is below.  
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a gushing of blood comes, then it befits him to stop it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And he should not at all pierce with the flame, but cut like a knife.   
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it befits you to restrain it, and change to another; 
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you desire any vein of him, or you treat in his place the vein in the arm. 
elle apert manifestement;	It opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cauterize to the flame as we have said.  
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw out the arm so that you touch the place until you know the pulse; 
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with chalk, and then tie the arm, and cauterize the vein with a hot flame;  
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it then. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your hand lengthwise on top of it, then remove your hand if the blood is still flowing, which many times happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	bind his arm, and leave it so, and do not move it to the patient.  
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be wary, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not healed, and it bleeds, and the remedy is not present, then stop the artery if it opens, because the head of it. 
et estainche li sans.	and heal the wound.  
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a rind of fig, and make it smooth, and take one half and bind it well until the next day. 
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the wound heals, that is good.  
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, then cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding. 
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the healing is not always achieved in multiple situations due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.  
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein of the arm in the middle if helped so that it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said;  
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the healer to place it over the nerve that is below, and if it is not drawn too deep, he finds the nerve, and it swells, and his senses are numbed, and by chance may not heal. 
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve is open many times, and if it does not open in certain men because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you feel the vein with a sharp instrument. 
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And prick the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the cephalic if helped, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes; 
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to bleed by pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because it is the safest of all the veins, because it does not have an artery or a nerve. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not grieve if it fails the first time, and one begins again. 
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance swells the veins in some men, because one fails the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know about bleeding is that bloodletting is administered only for the sake of preserving health, and to prevent future illnesses; 
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and whether the bloodletting is done in one of the three veins that are or cut:  
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic,  faste, and basilica.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of  priests to gain, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must bleed him on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and in all times. 
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not behoove to bleed children until fourteen years, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Let not those over sixty years old bleed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it is done, it behooves them that he cleanse the bowels with a light clyster if they have much stool held back, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines superfluities corrupted harmful to the principal members. 
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	and do not bleed those who are too full of meat, nor those who are drunk, as long as they are so, nor dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if it gets worse after colic passion, and vomiting, and stomach upset, and multiplication of womb in woman, and labor, watching and fasting, and all that virtue, or by thing of the arm or from the body; 
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly the humors, if it is thick, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have their power; 
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly the blood, and heal you of the vein in the lower part or third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things; 
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be quiet and joyful, and let the vein to be healed be higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then restrain the linen above halfway, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the humors; 
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with hands, until the veins swell, and they feel them. 
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the vein with a drop of old oil, then place his finger from his left hand above that vein below its place a little where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not escape and let the iron pierce it.  
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee as cords when bleeding, and if to such that are full of windiness, so that when one puts upon the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he operates on the vein, it is too tight; therefore it is necessary that the bloodlettings be advised in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it's good
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If it is not so, then begin again a little below that place or where there is swelling, if the place is not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen, and the patient fears, let him leave it one or two days, and do not tie up the arm:  
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	For adventure there may come a boil.   
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter into a bath, then begin again the cauterization if it pleases him. 
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, or the blood comes subtly and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, then fire in that same opening all the flame directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And do this a little bit below, so that the place becomes swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Because this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place inflamed, do not begin the bleeding again, and put on a little bit of oil, because it closes the body's blood, and is mixed in this place the oil that the eye; 
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; 
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and the same thing applies and ointment of them, when it is put on the place;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so make it subtle the grease and separate when it is too thick.  
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens many times, even when it is not bled except for this time or the opening of the vein is small, then haste, and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and some hot, and strain one hour; 
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do these things after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days, no blackening or greening, so it does not harm him. 
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on nothing of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamine, mintarstre, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times abscesses and appearance at the vein of the basilica:  
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put therefore your hand on it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of the hand, then is that appearance bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore I warn you that you do not put on it anything of what we have said, because by chance in it without the artery; 
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but the one you make a dry plaster to harden the place, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red. 
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see it swollen, let it stay until it becomes thinner.  
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is thin and weak, and needs bloodletting, make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide. 
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it should be bled sparingly and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking. 
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safer from a decrease in blood and damage to nerves, and is better than bleeding long or widely.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body needs bloodletting, it is necessary to give them soft bread with pomegranate juice. 
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is feverish, treat it with blood III times or IV. And if it is of cold complexion, give it before the sore a softened bread in syrup of musk, or in syrup of honey aromatic with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pricks at the vein, after the outflow of much blood, then it behooves him to soak a sponge with broth of flesh and subtle aromatic syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the opening of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to empty his arm after the first vein, and he has strong flesh, so he heals seven hours after the first vein, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another side, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	Because it has much blood within the body that is already feverish, and brings fever;  
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is necessary to bleed a great quantity, and widen the opening as much as it will flow in portions; 
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then that you cleanse all the conditions of the sore, and place your hand upon its poultice when it is healing, so that death does not come in its place with portions, and this happens many times when the healer is negligent; 
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not proper when you see a separation of the arm, and cause blood to flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press upon it forcefully; 
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is curved, extend the arm fully, because this would be bad.  
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it rest until it heals the second time; 
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you will prick it with the tip of the flame, until the vein that is frozen has been opened up, and place on top the piece of cloth put in water, and press lightly.  
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it alone and do not restrain it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity is to draw blood a second time, then in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein emitting from the arm is bled in place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing it is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the joint is red; 
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then heal it now across, not wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and be healed well near the joint of the hand, and if the blood cannot flow out, then put the hand back in hot water, and leave it there until you have enough. 
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not bathe the hand in hot water, because one puts it in more in winter than in summer;  
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is safer from all other veins, that there is neither artery nor nerve in it. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:  
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and plunge it in hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if one sees it; 
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it entirely throughout, it does not grieve anything;  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too far in depth, because the nerves are beneath all bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the sinew is frozen in the wound, and cannot issue forth.  
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you will have treated of the blood as much as is necessary, so put on the vein oil and wool to sew firmly, and thus do for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of him in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have said to you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sap of the sophene is good for all ailments that are below the body, such as diseases of the leg, and retention of flowers, and disease of the hips, and thighs, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of his blood are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it burns, and ties above the joint of the foot. 
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins; 
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So blood is taken from the larger vein, or at the ankle, which is better.  
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and bleed across as when cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be unyielding. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the vein cannot be released, then put his foot in water, and let it drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bloodletting is needed for the first time, begin the second one above a finger-width, because the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the other foot equally.  
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle of pain, and its hurt is worth to the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the qualities of his blood are such that the patient enters into a bath and is strained above the ankle four fingers by twisting, because otherwise he does not open the vein. 
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, let the blood flow in all the ways that you can, and by crossing.  
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, because the veins are dry, and they are very full to hand men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, let the blood flow from any vein that opens or towards the heel of the foot, and toward the little toe, and ward off the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make as much bloodletting as you see, and then untie the band, and put cotton on it and strain it. 
ele est maintenant sanee.	She is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of leeching
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made of horns, or glass, or wood.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And ventilation is done according to two manners: 
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.  
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation which is without pricking is according to two manners: 
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is done with hot air, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation which is done by pricking and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places of the body, of which one is all in the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on the two ribs of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction cup below the chin; 
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction cup on the two shoulders;  
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup above the knees; 
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction cups in the two arms; 
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction cups on the two legs;  
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction cups on the two ankles;  
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken them at all, as one does with blood from a vein; 
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, as long as the whole body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness it must be suctioned, or by habit, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are such people who when they need to ventilate have a heavy head; 
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who bring fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness to the eyes; 
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who bring a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see by blood, and wounds, and deaths, and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed after three hours of the day, we command to be ventilated.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The vein of the muse helps with the great pain in the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not right that this should be after the evacuation of all the body; 
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in the place of the vein of the cephalic, and it is not right that those who are of cold constitution use it, or who have catarrh, because this does great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason it is not appropriate that the elderly use it, nor those who have or chief cold diseases. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower down out of fear of obliousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is worth it to the treatment of pain, and incision of the channel of the throat, and all, and to repletion. 
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is necessary to pull it out carefully, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause blockage in the stomach and heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventosations at the second ribs of the neck are worth it for pains in the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and to strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the vein of the basilica;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary that you command the patient to spread his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery and does not come a hemorrhage of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilations of under the chin are good for mouth disease, and for gum rot, and similar diseases that are in the mouth. 
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the place of the healthy lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for the illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The bloodletting of the veins is as good as three veins of the arm because it draws blood from these large veins.
