et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to let them be too deeply cut because the vein is naked of flesh and lies beneath nerves and arteries.  
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The leech which is on the rump is as good as hemorrhoids of the foundation and as diseases below, and it is necessary that the leech be large and of grain so that it has need to well suck. 
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it were subtle, it would break. 
et i fai grans plaies.	And it makes large wounds.  
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The leeches of the legs are applied openly because they draw blood from the whole body and are as good as old pains in the hips, and of the groin, and of the bladder, and soften the tumors.   
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in place of the two shoulders, and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring pain in many positions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and then succeed temperately, and place it smoothly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing this until you see the place red and inflated, and appear the redness of blood. 
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then fire it, and put back the suction cups, and take care in the arrangement of the bodies, because there are some who have tender flesh and clear pores. 
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to make an incision only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a deep poke.  
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the flesh is thick, it is necessary to cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to subtilize the way of thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to prick the third time;  
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out blood little by little, then we only prick once.   
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we often begin again; 
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, prick it deeper, and the end of this is that the veins are pierced soundly, and it behooves him who has thick and hard skin, and whose pores are closed, that you oil their legs with ointments  of oil aperitif and dissolvent: 
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in the estate of skin, with oil of violets, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of gourd seeds; 
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in the estate of summer, with oil of watercress, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.   
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take oil of amber, or of balm, or of anise, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one to whom one is healing has tender skin and large pores, there it does not behoove to put any oil, but it behoves to wash after the ventosation of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rise from it, or from water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities should drink from old wine, or from the water of the cypress, or from a decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar. 
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And they should not apply a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours. 
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he bathe when he must be cupped, and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are being treated with cupping if they are choleric, and if their skin is too red and inflamed; 
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then it is necessary that they eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce with the leaves, and similar things; 
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced pigeons, and roast meat, and moist meats.  
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, takes syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and minced quince, and minced pears and small onions and pigeons;  
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will be treated, he should drink more than eat. 
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to certain men no times triacle or musket before the ventosation, or after, to comfort the principal limbs; 
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle with the herbs, but it is not proper that those who are hot drink them.  
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses that are applied without hurting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the knee, and gout, and on the belly and groin and flanks and hip, because these members do not suffer being hurt on themselves, and it is done only to draw blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the milk flows.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and groin to diminish the member. 
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or displaces the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus it is done when it is placed upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only so much.  
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water to which herbs suitable for this have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered to fire is here:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should have two sides and half a palm in width, and should have a small hole in the middle of the side, as for inserting a needle, and should be made of silver, so that before it is put on the limb it does not burn the patient; 
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle it should have a transverse bar of silver or iron, for placing a burning candle, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and the persons who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suckings of children are other than those of old people, and of the thin ones than of the fat ones. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one thus place this suction cup on the limb: 
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Taking the candle of wax or linen, and placing it within the suction cup through the rod which is within the suction cup, so that the clarity be at the bottom of the suction cup that it not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it upon the limb, and these must be on the opening that we have said, so that when one wants to, then there goes the vapor, and one removes the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take the linen as before, and recommence it often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup which is administered in illness of pleurisy, to all acute [illnesses], has no rod nor opening, and is administered only when it is full of water, and is placed upon the limb solely;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suctions are not administered except in members where one cannot place suction cups due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones. 
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in their skinless flesh, such as the two or one and others similar.  
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the qualities of the user is that when you find suctions which are in clear sweet waters without  damage, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them one by one in sweet water until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; 
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be healthy of vein and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the suctions.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they will be flat, and fall, if it is their place where one can put a suction cup, put it, because this works well after. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place with ease, and then with water, very well, and then tighten it. 
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if their sores are still healing too much after the flesh of the wounds, then moisten the linen cloth in cold water and put it on top, until the wound is healed. 
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wounds are multiplied, then put crushed vitriol or galena and similar things on top, until they are healed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and let them stay there until they dry out on the place, it will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other sores.  
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the blisters do not want to be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or put a needle there until the blister rises, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will swell; 
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bursting, put powder on a bit of aloe and silk ground together, or ash, so now they will heal. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the fools who look to this chapter and do not see anything in any of the ancient books or letters read;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is held back knowledge in our land, because I never found any good one; 
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; 
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are made, as I have done in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing hinders it, such as weakness of body, or child, or old man; 
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the thread is not very tight, or too cold; 
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and wear cold clothes, that is to say, cold clothing, and venison, lamb, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not stuff yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have a doubt of a hot abscess, or an expansion of matter in the limb; 
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to his first condition that he used.  
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great swelling, or that have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and eggs, and kidneys, and entrails, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such a cracking of the bone, it takes more time to heal and the fracture is faster
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that old and decrepit broken bones do not well mend or unite according to their nature for the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, like the bones of little children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but if there is a cure, reset the broken bone with the greatest care and join the limb together as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not let any point of his work, and for this reason he should be nourished with large meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or arm, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to a roll, and others that sharpen like the point of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with a fracture there is a wound, and a fracture to all a little fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to each manner of thing have its engine and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes in its place; 
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known the fracture of the bone by that which the parts are twisted, and open well by outside, and sound at the pressure of the hand; 
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no torsion nor sound at the touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; 
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not appropriate for you to move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes in arch, and are the II parts disjointed, it behooves them now to put at point equally, so that abscesses come from it. 
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if boils come to him, let him not touch them at all until they are quieted;  
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set him straight as you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of one who has pieces.  
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then restrain him, as it is fitting hereafter. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone it is broken in two parts, whether it be hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or to two cords, or to one cord and at your hand; 
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you put back all the additions in their places as best you can, and keep that by your work no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well.  
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it is well aligned, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who bring it by their work abscess hot and contraction of the limb, as we have wanted many times. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, so instruct the patient well that he does not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and watch well that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain at all. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and it behoves to put it in such disposition that it feels no pain; 
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And guard that it is placed straightly, so that twisting does not come when it is restored. 
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things: 
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is fitting to envelop them in linen wraps that are soft and fine;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are thick, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is fitting to envelop them in a wide and stiff linen, because the wide linens enclose the entire large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie bandages lightly around it, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on all of the linen, then go above the break and tighten less so that the break is slightly further apart.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you grab a large part of its healthy place, then take back the other ligament, and turn it straight again over the broken place. 
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, neither too hard nor too softly, as we have said in the first place above; 
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligaments compresses of linen or cloth, until it is all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or swelling, put on top something that soothes the abscess hot, and which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days; 
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then restrain with your splints, and be of half the width of a good-sized cane skillfully cut, or of wood from which they make cleavers, or of palm ribs, and be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the splint put on a fracture be somewhat larger and wider than the others; 
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as is fitting to the limb of small or large size; 
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on the splints just as you did in the first hour, then tie them above with thread evenly, as in the first hour above the fracture;  
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter is better above, less below; 
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too fine, and be of soft linen;  
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I wish in works of fools who make their bandages with cords of twisted linen, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have between each splint less than two fingers' width of space.  
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore by the joints of the shoulders after the straining in their healthy places, then put beneath them pads of linen, or wool cloth, so that he does not become bruised.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the bones are broken, I will say its cure here afterward.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is great, it does not behoove to put splints for after 5 days or 7, or more according to your certainty of abscesses following.   
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: 
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take flour that is held at the walls of the mill, and you combine it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, not too light nor too thick, and in use, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many ways, and also to women and to small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: 
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take three pounds each of abrasives, ladanum, rue, asafetida, and gum arabic, ten ounces each. 
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, five ounces 
alechil VIIII З.;	alechil nine ounces  
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix them with the white of an egg; 
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is hot, he should use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and has helped many men.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of plaster that is good for sprains: 
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and wormwood, ten ounces each;  
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, nine ounces each; 
acaice VI З.;	acacia six ounces 
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	and boil Armenian bole ten ounces, and grind it well, and mix it with water or the white of an egg, and administer it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothes the pain that occurs, and those who suffer from bone-setting, and fractures: 
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, and moisten it in vinegar and oil, and place it on the wound. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of setting a broken bone:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remaining pus from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of vervain, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of quince, one part each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind it, and confiture with wine, and if the limb is burned, confiture with coriander water, or plain water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of splinting more forcefully than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of vervain, flax seeds, balm, melilot, and henbane, and violet and chamomile flowers, one part each;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And grind, and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.  
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrates says in his book that on the broken limb one should put a restorative made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one must put on the broken limb, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to treat an injury that is worth pain: 
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and heads of garlic decapitated, or feathers of the eyes, and wormwood, and seal equally, and grind them, and make a poultice with them and apply it.  
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor has their bone moved from its place; 
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	then do not loosen it for many days.  
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, no rest, or swelling, then hasten, and loosen it, and remove the poultice now; 
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light cloth, and damp sea sponge, and dip it in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; 
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a bandage, until you are sure of the hot abscess.  
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then start the fine bandage again, and a little bit of emplastrum, and do not bind it as tightly as before; 
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be subtle until it is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and painful and swollen, I have removed it completely, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, if it starts again, as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, then do not untie it before after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for XX days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and the alignment of the bone approaches.  
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	therefore restrain it more than before, and make its flesh grow thicker, as I have said before; 
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see it drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there.  
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply therefore hot water to it, whenever you loosen it, and every third day, and moisten it a little. 
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this method therefore nourishment comes to the limb, and it mends quickly those who foolishly perform the opposite, which leave the limb twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and such work is perilous, and I do not see anything else but to let it be and operate it straightly.  
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse manners of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures there are, and diverse forms, and the causes are destined. 
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the thrust of a sword, and the bone breaks all the way to the side which is below the bone, just as it is done with an axe or club. 
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haiche".  
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; 
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound of these two fractures great or small.  
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow embedded, or fissure or of collarbone of stone, or of cheek on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating, which approaches to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound which is rejoined in the bone as subtle as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound which is made either by striking with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of bone inwards, and the lesion is like that which make the smith when he strikes on the cauldrons; 
si entre li piere dedens.	If among the stones within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft or damp bones, such as children's bones;  
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like splinters. 
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about them in their place.  
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all ways of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquiry at tents, and by the rotten cartilage which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair capillary is known by those who when one has uncovered the bone, and rubbed against it, so the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes is to be red and inflamed, and other similar ones in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no danger of accidents, and you hope for salvation, so begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, so hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day,  so that the tissue under the bone may be corrupted, and come the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture reaches up to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the fractured part as follows: 
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you shave the head of the patient carefully, and uncover the bone in every way that you can, and on the figure of the wound more softly than you can, and if blood comes out when uncovering the bone, or abscess form, then help with what is necessary, and that you fill the space with soft cloths in rose oil; 
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and be assured of bleeding cessation; 
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to cut around the bone to remove it, and it is done in two ways of work:  
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is that you cut with a narrow incision before, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts another piece larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is that you have a number of incisions of various widths, some narrow and others wide, and be pointed, and be of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in working lightly, that you do not bleed the head.  
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and stiff, it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer incisions with chisels, not by force that it does not penetrate beyond the bone of the test, and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;  
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have many of them, so that each comes in its place from the species of bone, so that you may have targets for all tests.  
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three ways of targets: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for perceiving around the broken bone is that you place one target on the bone, and turn to your two (sides) as long as you know that the bone is pierced. 
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the other target elsewhere a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and keep that you do not touch the marrow nor the sac.  
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and treated, it is necessary that you reset the apparatus which is dislodged from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tempered and more subtle than the other incisors; 
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there remain nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then lightly lift the bone with instruments; 
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then cure the wound with tents and dressings as we have said.  
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of working is that which Galen says, which is more dry; 
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it is said to be very powerful, and this is his word.   
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put below the head of this lens-shaped incisor, because this is its form.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and let the parted be sharp in two sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently chop the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane which is underneath.  
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is caught on the bone, gently pull on it, because pulling it easily does not harm and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce to the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to apply that rasping, and remove the flakes with a fine scraper which you must have various quantities, to administer in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If one shaves before with coarse razors, and after with more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, you must bring about a cause according to its treatment;  
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that is not fully replied to by anyone who has put their study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary that you place a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound. 
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this more gently than you can, that you don't hurt the wound, then administer above another linen cloth, and don't bind it too tightly except that it holds the wound alone; 
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let him so for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lily, and flour of quince, and incense powder, and astrology, and similar things. 
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put on the wound, and administer other medicines moderate without mortification;  
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound be always clean, that you do not leave any ointment, nor allow it to gather pus, because when pus gathers on the brain tissue, it decays and brings great harm to the patient; 
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	because when one puts on the above mentioned thing mordanting, it corrodes from above.   
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take therefore, if no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, then it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if pus does not come out forcefully but only from the medicine that has been applied, which has this virtue, then you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil, and glue one cloth, and put it on the wound;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure of manners of cures that it is necessary until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the upper bone, or one by itself, are broken because there are two bones. 
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that lower one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless forced to bend or twist, and then it heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you put your little finger or pointed finger into the bone and put equal to the broken piece in your index finger, and with the thumb from outside, until the bone returns according to its natural shape; 
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain by your work.  
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and it cannot come to its place, then you must set it equal at the head of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do this again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; 
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then place a poultice on the head with two layers of linen cloth if the fracture is in one part.  
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you put the other (poultice) on the other side, if the fracture is there; 
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the layers be so large that they fill the space of the two.  
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any restorer one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the making with eggshell powder and powdered millet;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the poultice, as long as the bone is hard and the cartilage has hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never put goose feathers in their place, and if the cloth is wrapped around it, and it holds the fracture, and it blows for the patient. 
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make how you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil comes while you are working on it, put some cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in the place of diaquillon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses come there, put a plaster from outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, congealed with egg yolk, then put light bandages on top, and bind nothing nor the sides;  
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the bones is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments to that end, then stitch the fissure, and cure it with things like charred flesh and ointment, and bandages, as suitable plasters and ointments for that purpose;  
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the bones, then cure it with bandages, and put some pieces of wool in it, until it is healed.  
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated down, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outwardly so, and not broken in two, except that it buckles inward, if one knows lightly of it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, that you put your left index finger in the mouth of the patient;   
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, put your right index finger inside and gently push the fracture inward, and hold it with the other hand from outside, and make it even. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension of the two parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	and if there is a movement of the teeth or a rupture, then restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and then place on the broken jaw a cerate, and put on top a double bandage. 
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on top of the bandage a large splint well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above where you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape is changing, then untie it on the third day, and then reset what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with abundance of egg or sesame flour, after what you have removed the cerate.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on a light linen plaster, and if the plasters adhere, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as it is sound 
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times it heals in III weeks.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, rewind that no piece of the bone is removed; 
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtle tools are used, suitable for those.  
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, so sew up the wound if it is wide, and place upon it plasters suitable to those, in order to prevent suppuration, until it be healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The shoulder breaks many times before, towards the shoulder blade, and the fracture is according to III manners: 
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and dislocated in II, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work if the fracture is without a wound, is that you have II ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the broken forcele;  
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the others extend the neck toward the part; 
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put each broken piece together so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance nor displacement. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth, or wool, and be as large as your necessity. 
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and gently raise the strength, and strain the ball with your hand so that you put each broken piece together as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus with force because it comes in contact, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his arm and put under the shoulder the pillow medium, and throw the ministers the shoulder down, until the bone of the humerus be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then bring the broken pieces together, and if you find them broken, then it is fitting that you cut further;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and try to bring the pieces together gently, and if the bone cannot join for any movement, then cut with one of the incisions you have made; 
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you place under the forceps this instrument, to guard the shaft
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and seems like a spoon, and is not at all curved, and be as wide as it convenes, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work. 
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, as you see, and one be wide, and the other narrow, like is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones. 
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of hot abscess, so close the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt hot abscess, so apply the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes to it, then soak the cloth in rose oil and wine, and put it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The strapping of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of ground meal and yolk of egg, and put light dressings over, and put a sphere under the saddle, if you have need. 
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide band, one palm's width, then put it doubled over the poultice, and fasten it. 
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender strip, three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandaged one, so that the head of the bandage hangs down.  
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and below the healthy shoulder, and below the injured shoulder;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the head does not move above the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligament loosens, then restrain it; 
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps put a small cushion under his buttocks, to raise the shoulder higher. 
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	So it will lighten the fracture of the shoulder blade by aligning the shoulder. You should bind his arm to his neck, and do not unbind it unless a bad accident happens, until twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then begin the splint again if you see that he needs it, and restrain it and leave him so until it is restored. 
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and in fewer for no man.  
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the shoulder breaks or gets wide open in the middle, and it is known only by touch.  
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you set the bone according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can.  
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on top of the place powdered flour with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on top a double cloth. 
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on top a wide and subtle board, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the edge of the board is chafing in any place of the shoulder, then use that hair (or fiber) for bandages of linen so that the board sits evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then restrain it with a whole great band firmly, so that the board does not move from its place, and check the linen every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it loosens, restrain it, and put the bone back in its place if it is out of position, and lay the patient on their side.  
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five. 
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is accomplished, untie it, and be sure, because it is not bone that moves easily out of place. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and not under the heart, do it as above, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the thigh to appease an abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone sometimes breaks in the middle, but it happens rarely.  
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks down to the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of alacrity, and thirst, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the seams in the broken bone, and he feels all bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and you put one cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs of the two ribcages with your hands, and subtly try to set it in every way that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; 
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put on plasters and poultices above the subtle salt cloth, or another light cloth, and wrap it in a bandage, and place it on the broken bone so that it does not move. 
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And turn the limb around to the back, and restrain it tightly, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it softens, tighten it. 
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it is necessary to loosen it, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, remove the plaster, and address what has come there with ways of treatment; 
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reapply the bandage, and restrain it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of the ribs comes only in their thick part after the back, and at the top inside, and they bend only because they are brittle;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he feels it well at the examination as two. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint, and restrain it with a strap, if you need it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is declining inwards, the patient feels great pain and a sharp sensation, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung; 
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and besides pain, and coughs and vomiting great quantities of blood, and this is a grievous ailment, and the ancients have put great effort into it.  
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, in order to expel the wind outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not perform this, except abscesses are present if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to him, heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said any of you should apply cupping to the area, to suck out the pus and this seems reasonable; 
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping draws away superfluous substances from the area because of weakness.  
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say none of us should cover the place with soft wool in hot oil, and put a tent between the ribs to make the wound even, then it is cured by the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone piercing the lung, and there is doubt about the patient, it is necessary to cut above the site of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under the instrument in order to guard the wound;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And therefore one must dig the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a boil comes, put it on cloths moistened in rose oil, and put it on the spot; 
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the place of that which is fitting for the boil, and lie still on his side or where it should be, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bone of the neck, and sometimes it happens that he bends;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if he will be healed or not, if you take notice if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he feels nothing.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many positions, and if they move and feel well when they are restrained and pulled, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if one puts care to it.
