Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take notice if his feet are softened, and if the accident is in his hands, and on his back there is windiness and involuntary excretion; 
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one is healing it upon his belly, there jumps forth an evacuation without volition.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and he wants to sit, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal: 
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if one does not labor well in its care.  
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, so place upon the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is appeased; 
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put upon one of the comforting and drying plasters, and tie it with a linen bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; 
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes disjointed, then it is necessary to cover upon the heart; 
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one suture, then cure it with ointment that incites flesh, until it is healed; 
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the hip", put your pouch in your left hand, and make it even with the other hand as you can, then put the splint and support on top, if you need it; 
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then restrain it, and if there are bones displaced, set them in place, and treat the wound until it is healed.  
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes it happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there may be only a little bit of lessening at the head;  
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and then it lengthens and leans towards the outside, and comes to the patient pain in that place, and prickling, and swelling where it breaks. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know which are the fracture and the form of them; 
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is in the head alone, then set the fracture even, as long as it is in natural form. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it bends inwards, then make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, then put on the plaster, then put on a splint of wood or of cork, and restrain the fracture so that it does not move; 
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the weight under the ribs, as long as the ligament is even.  
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes there, then do not touch it, as long as the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as is fitting, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistant is what is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two ways: 
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a thick rod of wood, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two heads with two bindings, and bend them upward, and set the patient on the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then lay the broken arm on the rod, until it reaches the armpit, and has in its middle a curve of wood, then place on any heavy thing or the ministers stretch it downward; 
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the two ends of the fracture together with his hands, until the fracture returns as it should.  
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one supports the patient on his bed, and binds his hand to his neck, then commands his ministers that one holds that which is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below to all the limb, and extends each one to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, restrain the linen below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each minister to its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one binding below the armpit, and the other toward the elbow, below the fracture; 
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And also if the fracture is towards the outside, it is necessary to put the splint lightly, without effort, until the fracture is equal on the surface and on the outside. 
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the fracture as it should be, and restrain it, if a boil does not come there.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if a boil comes there, do not restrain it until the seventh day, and put on moistened linen in oil of roses, until the boil is appeased.  
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you put the splint on the fracture, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage, and restrain on the shoulder and on the arm so that the arm is in a straight line, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.   
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use splints, and put on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one finger's width of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the fracture three fingers on each side; 
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then bind upon the splints, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, tighter and less spreading outward. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the placement of the splints, and the binding, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it bound up until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at the joint every three days, that it does not itch or swell, or that the nurse can come to the limb for this reason because it is too sore. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if none of those accidents come, then do not unbind it before three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach. 
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the shoulder one cushion plain of wool equally, and look each hour of the day or of the night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or is softened the ligatures.  
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If you address him by the power of medicine, and give him the meat that we have placed before, in such a way that the meat is first finely ground.  
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And when he begins to recover, it should be coarse. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days from all;  
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must unbind it and administer baths and medicaments of ointments for the place to be healed. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and entangled, it remains to untie for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fossils," because one is small, and that is the one that follows the armpit;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little toe; 
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance breaks the large fossil alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.  
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing.  
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large ones are broken, so is the healing bad, and more painful than when they are broken together.  
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended, and set straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's the large bone, then it should be restrained more strongly. 
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	And place it on the cushion and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the other bones, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor. 
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the ministers (ministers) of his arm to the underside of his hand, or to the linen, and some other ministers to the other above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if any are severed that grip the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make it up with bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; 
si pren la cure.	If you take care of it.  
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration boils appear, then glue a patch of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, that it is neither too hard nor too soft. 
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and cover the patch gently, until the boils are appeased.  
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cerote, and put the ointment of ground flour with abundance of egg on it, then place the bandages, and let the bandage of the splint be more to the outside, and a little wider than the others.  
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	And know that it must have six bandages or arms in more ways. 
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	And bind more above the fracture than elsewhere, and all days less away from it, as I said at the beginning of the chapter. 
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages that are on the wound be soft and moist, and not hard or rough.  
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, with which it is stitched, be of linen, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said.  
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you bathe the limb in hot water until the itch is appeased. 
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be too tightly bandaged resting.  
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are loose and the bones out of place, and similar things, so address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And take care if the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too far away, then you must soften it a little, and leave it so for some days, until the nourishment comes back, and then restrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not unbind him until XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or if he does so then let him place his hands to his neck, and let his arms be level, and beware of movement and fidgeting, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And know that this wound is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty, according to the constitutions and the complexities of the virtues.  
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on our wrists many fractures occur, and there comes nothing but swelling many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient lie crossed, and be straight in front of him equally. 
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then put his hand on the board stretched out, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them equally the eyes, until they are well joined.  
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And put the plaster and the bandages, if an abscess does not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place.  
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And be enveloped in a linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the end of the hand toward the belly, make a sphere of cloths, and command the patient to tighten it to his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then the constraint of a long cloth, and let the star of the heart be as large as the palm of the hand, and the constraint, as it is necessary. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie tightly around the hand, and make the bandage tight between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of our two sides, if it is the pouches, set it equal, as it is necessary. 
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and restrain with the palm, and if you see to put a small straight star to raise the fracture, and do not move it. 
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is to the other two, as in the index or one of the others, set it equal, and tie it with the healthy joint which is after. 
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all in I holding, that much worth, or you put on a star, as in the pouch;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take ward in the restoration and in the arrangement of hot abscesses, and cure those that come, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is many times broken, and one sees it well when it turns forward and backward. 
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration if is done by tying one above the fracture, and the other below.  
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then extend each minister his tie evenly; 
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is joined of the bone.  
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, so one of the ligaments toward the groin, and the other ligaments below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the tie be below the knee, and let the extension be downward; 
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the mirages bone evenly with his two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the plaster, and the tie, if an abscess does not come.  
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it be appeased then return to your work and your cure; 
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The ligament is made in such a manner.  
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you encircle the fracture with a rigid bandage doubled in II or III, and remove the superfluities, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put the long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the end of the thread upward. 
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn upwards on the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put above the fracture splints, and put a splint above the bone of the leg; 
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then employ the place eight between the leg and the hip of cloths soft to put equal pressure, then begin to bind in the form III twists or IV above the fracture; 
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go higher above the fracture, and less restrain it; 
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then feel for the two bones of the thigh that you have put between the leg and the hip, and in part III are the small bones above, then go back down to the bottom of the thread, until you reach near the foot.  
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and restrain it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that there comes no abscess or swelling nor any other sign. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens there, untie it, and address what comes out, as we have said many times. 
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that grasp, then it is necessary to remove them, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it is necessary to split the place and drain pus.  
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the hip is broken like this, when it is set, like in the shoulder or arm. 
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Nevertheless, with restoration done like this, it does not help the patient. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And knows that the hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the path of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer just a fissure, or perforation, and it happens to every wound, and without wound, and this one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is done by putting equal those things that are rounded to their sides, as long as they can be assembled and moved together. 
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then put the splint on it and put a round piece of wood inside if you need it, and restrain it as is fitting, then follow all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, like a hot poultice and something similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put to each accident what is fitting for it, until it is healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called by right "the fibula," and the other is called "the tibia." 
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And there happens every breakage as it comes to the arm, and for that reason, the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all here. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.  
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is seen well; 
et torne desoz.	and it turns downwards.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Therefore administer extension, and put it straight, and tie the splints equally; 
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, it is necessary if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; 
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the splint according to its virtue.  
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have accomplished your work entirely, take two strips of  wooded splint that support the leg on one side and the other, and be the length of the leg from the knee down below; 
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap it in two bands above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and with this bandage, the leg will not be able to bend to the right or left, and thus it is good. 
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer anything to the long bone of the leg, and if it is broken, put on the leg in order to ward off movement, and this is properly done in the fracture or where there is a wound. 
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or any other accident; 
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it cures as long as it is healthy.  
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but to the bones of the foot come at any time fractures and to two points, and there have been further than in more postures.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if the bones of the foot are broken, and you see these bones overlap each other, put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it so that they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put the splint and bandages on top, and put under the belly of the foot a small board at the two shoulder blades, then restrain it to the foot carefully, then that you have wrapped with cloths around, and other things which you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when III days or IIII will have passed, then untie the linen, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any of the two broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers of the hand;  
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and be one point more wide, then put under the foot that board that I have said, and restrain it carefully; 
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each finger a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and restrain the board under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And let it stand on the top of the board further out under the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.  
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, since we have said them. 
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it is fitting.  
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the break of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, set it standing wide open, then incline it to the back part, and have it held by the back; 
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the hollow of the woman's body with cotton, and put in as much as I stand for; 
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then lift the woman up, and raise her back gently, gently, and then push the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the body, and return the bone with the stand;  
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, take away the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or around: 
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	then the fracture will be restored, and if you see it, take a sheep bladder, and tie a string to the opening, and put the whole bladder into nature;  
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the string end, until the bladder is inflated inside: 
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will return the fracture;  
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the finger of a man or a woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; 
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures near are not hidden from him who sets his study and practice to it, and understands my book.  
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies to more than one disposition the right way of restoration: 
enten le donques.	Therefore, then.  
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the thigh; 
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloths around it, and leave it there for three days or until it is healed, and it will be healed without haste. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the wounds that we have said testify to them.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, keep the vitriol there, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the broken bone that same hour, or that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come there, let the restoration remain until the ninth day, so long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it neither on the third nor on the fourth day, for you would make it come bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered chest, then it behooves you to set it gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not ready for you to put it even with your hands, then take this instrument which is of iron, which is seven or eight long, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this purpose you must make sure that it is impregnated with three or four, according to what he needs in each cure of fracture; 
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and be round and about an inch thick, so that it does not bend at the compression on the limb during your work, and be blunt in front, and thicker from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And is called "palangin," for which the head of the bone should be placed on top of the apparent bone.  
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And bring it together at once, until it returns, and are equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it behooves you to chop the head of the bone, until the instruments have purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then with an instrument suitable for this, or scalpel or saw, to your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then raise what is remaining in the bone of sharpness and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	So do until it is in its place, then moisten the bandage with black wine stich and properly if this is in situation;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound, other than to which there is oil, lest it cause decay and corruption. 
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and give yourself good guard that the wound is not strained with the fracture. 
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have these things happened to the foolish people, and they have brought upon the patient either death or corruption at any time;  
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And let the constriction be softer and more gentle than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may occur there, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it does not behoove to put upon stars.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, in place of stars, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, remove what you have placed on top of all the wine, and put ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmasion and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the bone comes down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days it passes and it cannot be mended back in place, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must close the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder, and similar ones of the large limbs, do not touch it, for many times death may come from it, but let it be until it will heal itself;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps after twenty days or thirty it will fall by itself, then you can cure the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it so. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We come often after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is a sad thing to see the figure of the limb; 
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance, he cannot do the natural works of his limbs.  
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take guard therefore if it seems to us fresh: 
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he administers medications astringent, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acai, and similar others, in the way that you take any of these things, or all together, and you confit them with astringent wine or with yolk of egg or with honey; 
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the wound as poultices, and bind it well, and do not separate it in hands for days; 
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then unwrap it, and begin another one, as long as the swellings are removed;  
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you restrain upon a piece of plank well made; 
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the properties of the plank are that it removes all the swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then make a cut above, and bring the superfluity to appear.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you apply it to a certain razor, until it is removed, and the wound heals. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains afterward the limbs weak and thin, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one reason being because it was bound too tight, and not bound as it should be; 
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and the blood supply could not come to the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or by a multitude of blows; 
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or by too great movements, not at its proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, he is weak 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood is multiplied in him. 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths to him, and give him joy and ease; 
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put the poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the rose often with warm water, until the swelling corrects to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After health, the crooked limb
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	so do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; 
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and by chance death. 
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the knots and the tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be risen with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of balm, and roots, and melilot, and similar things. 
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply a softening plaster, such as diachylon well made, and take the mucilage of balm, and confit it with fat of goose or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top. 
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take figs, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.  
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and lengthwise with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the torments are old and hardened, like stones, and there is a need to remove them with iron, then it is necessary to cut to the bone, with a subtle incisor lightly.  
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put cushions and study in the cure. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is an issue from any joint of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is badly formed, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, then it is necessary now to bring back without tarrying.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, then the limbs swell, and by chance if one sets it back with force; 
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	for this it is not necessary to move it when it is inflamed 
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times brings pain and other aches;  
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	However, when this happens, if you make the patient healthy, then let him be, as long as the abscesses are calmed; 
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each member as they come back to their place.  
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It happens that the jaws are dislocated and the dislocations of both are according to II manners: 
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are a little out of place, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chin, and close the saliva from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and surrounds his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by many disarrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then it is necessary that you reset it carefully, and do not hesitate at all. 
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the patient, and put his fist into the pocket from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; 
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other hand should be outside, to make them equal.  
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And command the patient that he soften his mandibles and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the member is placed evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is brought back with a grip, even if it is the two mandibles together, then apply hot water and oil, until they are gently reset. 
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not hesitate about resetting, as we have said.  
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset equally, and the patient's mouth is well closed without softening, then place a moistened cloth on a felt made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with soft bands. 
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient sleeps on his back, and his shoulders be standing between two pillows, so that he does not move them to the right or to the left, nor does he make any effort to speak, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are healed. 
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then he chews what he wants lightly, and does not make any effort to open his mouth when eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and sound.  
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set back in place within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and familiar fevers come, and perhaps a bowel rupture, and perhaps vomiting of cold phlegm.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a peril.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And many times die those who have it, in nine days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The wrench cannot dislocate from within the ribcage, continuing into the flank, and it is dislocated no times outwardly, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and stretches out his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then presses the place with the palm of your hand, and it will return. 
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then place on the splint and the bandage, and restrain.  
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the shoulder which is towards the side cannot dislocate. 
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does, and if it dislocates again at any time, reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place on the splint and the bandage, and restrain it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; 
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same way, bring back the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in only three ways: 
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	of which one is that it dislocates towards the hip.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is towards the chest; 
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance, it dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely.  
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the nerves.  
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And many times it dislocates downwards towards the seat, even to those who have little flesh, because at them it is felt harder; 
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	To those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.   
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men a percussion or fracture, and inflates the shoulder with a hot abscess, and believes that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore it behoves that you prove it, as long as you are certain of it; 
et adonques encomence la cure.	And then begin the cure.  
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known the dislocation when it is pulled downwards towards the seat, and puts a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity; 
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the seat touching the top of the shoulder, as if they were one piece;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its place, nor move it in any way; 
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you can clearly feel it by touch; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not difficult to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is healthy.  
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person upwards, then put their hands under the armpit, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place; 
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upwards, then put it downwards; 
si venra hastanment.	so they come together gently.  
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come together as we have said in hand shortly after, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And the minister soothing and comforting ointment, as decoction of altea and fennel and melilot in water, and be administered. 
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then be the patient laid on his back, and put under his buttock a piece of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then place his heel on the cloth, and lift the shoulder's head gently, and draw the hand of the ill. 
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	And another minister holds the head of the patient, so that it does not move down;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder returns now all, and if you see so reset it according to this manner: 
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you make be present a man who is greater than the sick.  
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight toward the ribs, and push the shoulder below the seat of the sick, and lift the seat up, so that the sick person hangs in the air; 
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other ministers pull the hand of the sick downward toward the belly.  
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may put with him any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reset it also in another manner: 
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and is on puts a long stick in the earth, whose head be as also as the post, and be neither too thick nor too slender;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	Then let the patient lie down, but that he have coverings on top of him, and the patient be standing by the long staff. 
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then let his hand be stretched out to one side forming, and the joint will return to its place readily;  
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a piece of wood from the arm of great size and four inches wide, which has the head rounded to enter through the bottom of the sleeve, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie on top of the staff coverings so that the staff does not bruise the patient, then place it under the sleeve of the patient;  
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And extend his arm on top of the long staff, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm at the end of the hand, then place the arm on the edge of a plank of large size, and let the hands be extended down, and let the body hang down from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint returns now. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that it is, it behooves you to put under the shoulder cap a ball of wool even, then put the plaster sprinkled with powder of the mill, with incense and auburn of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then strain under the shoulder evenly, and turn the linen on the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he exercise little, as long as the limb is fortified, because it will heal more quickly; 
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then he should exercise more after seven days or so, and move it;  
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is hardened and not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is displaced from its place due to moisture that has come or for another cause, then you must administer cautery to it in three places, as it is shown in the chapter of cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or extended or softened; 
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in place.  
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the hip, and the breast, or back, it is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and there are administered other places;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care until it is sound. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing pain comes to the limb, and gradually in movement, so the patient uses baths many times, until that pain is soothed, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the knee is dislocated often and frequently returns.  
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated from all sides, both front and rear, and the dislocation is not well set, because one sees it well and feels it well; 
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocated according to each figure.  
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the blade with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it as the abscess comes, because if the abscess comes, it would be harmful to reset it;  
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the rear; 
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.   
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can reset it, that you extend your hand to both hands; 
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And his arms be spread out, and the hands do touch according to the knife around, in front and behind, and push the joint to its chest together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and grasps the root of the palm with his knife that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; 
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it tight so that it does not move during the extension; 
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, then that you have enveloped a double cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the fingers have joined the joint to its hand, then the oil of any oil for softening the joint, then push the joint firmly together, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, then put on a dry plaster with a drop of egg white, and hold it firmly together, and lean the arm to the neck of the patient, and let it for some days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the ligament, and leave it.  
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint is not well set, start again with the splint and the ligament, and leave it for some days, until it is firmly set. 
puis le deslie.	Then untie it.  
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe it and rub it well, and press it until it is soothed. 
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put on the joint a wool fleece, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and make him enter a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put on the fleece again, and then into the bath. 
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And thus do it two or three times until it is healed.  
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see it, put on top fine cloth moistened with hot butter, and keep it pressed. 
si revenra a sa disposition.	It will return to its place. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is easier than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place carefully, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the limbs do not swell, or that an abscess comes hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is that you put the diseased hand on a table, and extend the ministers the hand, and carefully place it equal, so that it places its palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns. 
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is necessary that you look if it is well in its place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then put the diseased one's back of his hand on a table at extension and return. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, the patient puts the back of his hand on the table, and the helper puts his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is well. 
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then strain with soothing plasters the abscess, and leave it so without recommencing.  
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in its place after several days, then the joint remains crooked. 
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and does not harm the patient except that as long as his hand is weak, and cannot pull anything at all. 
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	therefore know that the nerves are cut, or the artery;  
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other thing to do except to restrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is worth nothing else. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then hold it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and let it be as such.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, apply the hot water cloth, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the bones of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or the belly;  
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	therefore are the bones, and push the dislocation into your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the bone, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; 
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for a day, and then put it straight again that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bandage it, as we have said, and unbind it every day, and make it move, and then re-bandage it. 
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is straight, and also do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do so, when it is dislocated from another place. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs of this are that the members jump away without will, cannot hold them, and many times are softened any limb, or the two hips or the two arms or one. 
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times it moves the shoulder in four parts.
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	That which moves at the back is called "gilbosite": 
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure of this is that you reward oneself if the "gilbosite" comes from childhood:
