si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure nor healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those which come from a fall or percussion or similar things, the ancients said there were ways of treatment with great words, where there is little profit in all. 
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.  
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling which comes to the breast before, nothing heals. 
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also that which comes directly in the two sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say. 
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that the patient be stretched on his face in the equal place, and have a strain below him, that he does not move. 
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert the tinder at the head into the earth forming, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen around below the buttocks of the patient, and the other to the hips, and knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and the minister knows the ligaments, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bones.  
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the bone as we have said, and the minister puts his palms upon the spine, forming a shape, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board three arms long, and place it under the shoulder, and let the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the shoulder, then put the middle of the board upon the spine;  
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and let the minister place his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see, do so with the turnip that turns in the hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you put two bones at the head of the patient with one arm long, and towards the feet, other two, and have between each bone, above and below, a palm's width of length;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each stick a hole, or the turning goes, and be the sticks firmly in earth, so that they do not move. 
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two sticks have one turning stick, so that the line turns, and have in each turning two small sticks of a palm long, to turn the turning. 
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the line which is among the axles to the turning towards the head, and the other line towards the feet to the other turning, and each of the ministers turns his turning on the whole line, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.  
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on a drying plaster with plenty of egg white, and then the splints, and then the strip of a tablet of three fingers long, which covers the place of the vertebra and the part of the healthy spine, then tie it with a line as we have said, and use the patient to subtle nourishment, until he is healed; 
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if any thing comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the method that we have said before.  
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes it is administered a piece of sponge, and sometimes it appears in the back spine of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocation. 
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that opens, therefore one must not have presumption there.  
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	for adventure would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only with dislocations, and do not come out like other joints. 
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to IV parts:  
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more inside then, and poco dislocated in front and back. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens wider the knee of the injured than the healthy one, and the injured person cannot double their knee. 
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the limb that is below swollen with abscess heat, because of the coming of the hip joint. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to the fever, so is this accident contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who has this in front, it is that they are well their leg according to completion; 
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	However, they do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make them walk, they cannot before, and retains their urine, and swells the groin, and when they go, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has it in back, is that he cannot extend his knee nor double, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the hip joint is in place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The return of this kind of dislocation is that you notice if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, there is no cure;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And he should not have presumption there. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in this one whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of IV manners of dislocation, so hasten that you return the joint, and the extension within and without, and the movement to the right and left; 
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For perchance it will return, and there is no need for other cure.  
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you prepare the minister strongly, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or on the linen that is tied above the knee; 
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and other ministers extend their hand above in such a manner that they push their hands under their shoulders, then the tighten with a linen band above the hips;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another grip the head of the linen. 
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend upward and downward all at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.  
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this is not done, it is necessary to take care of its appearance. 
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is at the edge, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy rib, then put the linen on the root of the hip, and the place which is below the groin, then extend the linen upward toward the groin, and towards the strong muscle. 
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then grasp with other ministers his arms, and embrace the thick part of the diseased hip, and extend it outward.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	Then it will return to its place now; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.  
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the sick person together with a strong linen cloth above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; 
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then let it be hung from the top of a pole, and be above the ground two arms long;  
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command the minister to embrace the head of the groin, and let another minister be hanging with the sick person, who embraces the groin firmly, for the joint now returns quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the back, let the sick person lie down, as we have said in the one who has gimpiness, and restrain the linen on the sick leg properly, and on the foot also; 
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two sticks, one at the top and the other at the feet, then stick a stick between the hips of the sick person in the middle;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And have the patient wrapped in damp cloths so that he does not feel cold, then extend each minister towards him, and the surgeon puts his hand into the dislocation.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it is not, place on, that is, a table, and press as we have said in the chapter of the boil, and the patient lies on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as much as possible, and according to what I have said; 
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and put the surgeon's palm above the sick angle, then press with the other hand, and pull it down towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the sick one down, nor raise it up on the ground, but rather that it should be as if the hip had been dislocated backwards, as we have said about lying on the two hips; 
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And be upon its face, and the bandage is extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table. 
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	And it will be pointed when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even.  
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	Then adjust the hips, and put the splint, and the band of bandage so that the hip does not move. 
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	And rest three days or four, then untie it, and put the splint on top.  
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	And if you see that they are even, so bandage, as before, and leave it three days. 
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened.  
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways: 
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	That is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards. 
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislocate again 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if he does not hold it at his hip, know that it is dislocated; 
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; 
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your two hands, then bend the two bones that form the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he holds his leg at his hip lightly; 
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on top, and make the leg rest at the hip, and keep them together tightly for three days or four, then untie it; 
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and let the patient not try to walk, until the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tender before the part where it is dislocated: 
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The resetting is light, and one should extend it gently with his hands when it is only softened.  
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, then you should make the patient sit straight, and hold him firmly by the leg, above the ankle; 
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the foot in your right hand, and then in the left twice, then push it upward, and gently push the foot upward;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; 
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that is well;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, begin the work again, for it will return. 
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return like this, so do to guide the patient onto their back on the ground, and stick a pail firmly in the ground between their hips, and tie blankets around, that it does not cold the patient. 
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then grasp the ministers the hip, and another minister extends the foot to their hands or to the linen, that it ties above the neck of the foot. 
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend each minister equally, and the pail should be placed between the hips of the patient to hold the patient when it is extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the ministers equally the dislocation in their hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return gradually.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, so put the plaster and bandages on top, and hold firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are on the ankle behind, so that the linen is not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then let him leave it for two or three days, and if the bonds soften, then strain it. 
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for four days.  
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come there, then it is fitting that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them well without effort, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, then you should make the patient sit on a level surface or on a table perfectly straight, and place your foot upon what is apart from these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is aligned and there is nothing apart from it, then place beneath the sole of the foot a board two fingers wide, then strain it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it. 
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him rest, until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:  
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	So be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, nor too bold; 
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning soothing things to an abscess hot, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; 
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the limb now, so that the hot abscess may come;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to the hot abscess, and treat the wound as befits it, with dry dressings;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if it is accompanied by a fracture, and fractured bones are dislocated, then set the bones, and do what we have said in simple diseases. 
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And guard yourself from entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it brings you harm according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and body.
